Liability for Sprinkling Water on Part vs. Whole Road
Ruling on liability for road sprinkling with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rulings on daman for road obstructions based on the victim's intention and the extent of obstruction, and apply the principle of 'illa vs. sabab to similar cases.

Core Idea
Liability shifts from the sprinkler to the passerby if he deliberately steps on the wet part, but stays on the sprinkler if the entire road is wet.

This lesson examines a nuanced rule in Hanafi tort law: when a road-sprinkler causes a death, the ruling on liability depends on two factors: the victim's intention and the scope of the obstruction. You will learn how the concepts of effective cause ('illa) and compulsion (idtirar) determine who bears financial responsibility. The passage also extends the same distinction to placing planks on the road, illustrating qiyas in action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two distinct cases: (1) the road is only partially wet, and the passerby intentionally steps on the wet part; (2) the road is entirely wet. Identify the ruling for each.
2
Determine the effective cause ('illa)
Analyze why in the first case the sprinkler is not liable: the passerby's own deliberate act is the effective cause of his fall, not the water. In the second case, the sprinkler's act becomes the cause because the passerby had no choice (compulsion).
The Urdu commentary explains: 'illa is the free agent's act; sabab is a mere circumstance.
3
Understand the qila minority view
The text includes 'qila' (it is said) that the no-liability ruling applies only when part of the road is wet. This is a clarifying nuance, not a dispute; it reinforces that the distinction hinges on partial vs. full wetting.
Some Hanafi commentators consider this a mere specification of the general rule.
4
Apply qiyas to analogous cases
The author extends the same ruling to a plank placed on the road. Recognize that the effective cause ('illa) is the same: the victim's ability to avoid the obstacle. If the plank blocks the entire road, the placer is liable; if only part, and the victim deliberately steps on it, the placer is not liable.
The qiyas is explicit: 'wa kaza al-hukm' (and the same ruling applies).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص عمد آپانی کی جگہ سے گورا اور پھر گر کر مر گیا تو ضمان نہ ہوگا
ولو تعمد المرور في موضع صب الماء فسقط لا يضمن الراش لأنه صاحب علة وقيل هذا إذا رش بعض الطريق لأنه يجد موضعا للمرور ولا أثر للماء فيه فإذا تعمد المرور على موضع صب الماء مع علمه بذالك لم يكن على الراش شيء وإن رش جميع الطريق يضمن لأنه مضطر في المرور وكذا الحكم في الخشبة الموضوعة فى الطريق فى أخذها فى أخذها جميعه أو بــعــضــــه ترمہ اور اگر اس نے پانی گرنے کی جگہ گزرنے کا تعمد کیا ہے پس وہ گر گیا تو چھڑکنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ گذرنے والا صاحب علت ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ( عدم وجوب ضمان ) اس وقت ہے جب کہ وہ راستہ کے کچھ حصہ پر چھڑ کے اس لئے کہ ( گذرنے والا ) گذرنے کی جگہ پائے گا حالانکہ اس جگہ میں پانی کا اثر نہیں ہے پس جب اس نے ( گذرنے والے نے ) پانی گرنے کی جگہ پر سے گذرنے کا ارادہ کیا اس کے جانے کے باوجود اس کو (پانی گرنے کو) تو چھڑکاؤ کرنے والے پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اور اگر اس نے پورے راستہ پر چھڑکاؤ کیا تو وہ ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ ( گذرنے والا ) مرور میں مجبور ہے اور یہی حکم ہے راستہ میں رکھی ہوئی لکڑی میں لکڑی کے کھیرنے میں پورے راستہ کو یا بعض راستہ کو ۔
تشریح زید نے جہاں پانی چھڑ کا ہے وہ پورے راستہ پر نہیں ہے بلکہ کچھ راستہ پر ہے جہاں کو خالد گذ رسکتا ہے لیکن وہ قصد امونچھوں کو تاؤ دیتے ہوئے اس جگہ کو گذر رہا ہے جہاں پانی ہے تو زید پر منمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں گذر نیوالے کا فعل علت ہے اور چھٹر کئے والے مافعل سبب ہے۔ اور اصول یہ ہے کہ جب علت کے اندر یہ صلاحیت ہو کہ حکم کی اضافت اس کی طرف ہو سکے تو پھر سبب اور شرط پر ضمان نہیں ہوا کرتا اور یہاں مار کا فعل علت صالحہ ہے کیونکہ یہ فائل مختار کا فعل ہے (و فصلناه في درس الحسامی) ہاں اگر زید نے پورے راستہ میں پانی چھڑک رکھا ہے تو زید ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی ضرورت میں جانے کے لئے خالد مجبور تھا اور وہ زید کے فعل کی وجہ سے گر گیا اور مر گیا تو زید پر ضمان ہوگا۔
اسی طرح اگر زید نے راستہ میں لکڑیاں ڈال رکھی ہیں تو بھی یہی تفصیل اور حکم ہے۔
A person intentionally passed over a place where water was sprinkled, then fell and died; there is no liability. And if he intentionally passes over the place where water was poured and falls, the sprinkler is not liable because he (the passerby) is the one with the fault. It is said this applies only when he sprinkled part of the road because he can find a place to pass with no trace of water. Thus if he intentionally passes over the place of water with knowledge, there is nothing on the sprinkler. But if he sprinkled the entire road, he is liable because the passerby is compelled to pass. The same ruling applies to a plank placed on the road, whether it occupies the whole or part of it. Explanation: If Zaid sprinkled water not on the whole road but on a part, and Khalid could pass elsewhere but deliberately goes over the wet spot, Zaid is not liable because the passerby's act is the effective cause, and the sprinkler's act is only a cause. The principle: when the cause has the capacity to have the ruling attributed to it, liability does not attach to the mere condition or instrument. Here the passerby's act is a valid cause because it is the act of a free agent. However, if Zaid sprinkled the whole road, he is liable because Khalid was compelled to pass out of necessity and fell. The same distinction applies if wood is placed on the road.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability for causing death by sprinkling water on a road. The author states two scenarios: (1) If only part of the road is wet and the passerby deliberately steps on it knowing it is wet, the sprinkler is not liable because the passerby's own intentional act (the 'illa or effective cause) supersedes the sprinkler's act (merely a cause). (2) If the entire road is wet, the sprinkler is liable because the passerby had no alternative and is compelled to pass (mudtar). The same rule applies to placing a plank on the road. The Urdu commentary clarifies using the example of Zaid and Khalid: the principle is that when the victim's own free act is the direct cause, the original actor is not held liable. This is a key principle in Hanafi tort law distinguishing between cause (sabab) and effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for harm caused, specifically blood money (diyah) for death or property loss.
صاحب علة (sahib 'illa): A person whose own deliberate act is the direct cause of harm, making him responsible.
مضطر (mudtar): One who has no choice or alternative but to pass through the obstructed path, due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zaid sprinkles water on only half of a road, and Khalid deliberately steps on the wet part knowing it is wet, falls, and dies, who is liable?
A) Zaid is liable because his sprinkling caused the fall.
B) Khalid is liable because he intentionally stepped on the wet part.
C) Neither is liable.
D) Both are equally liable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tort law, liability for road obstructions hinges on whether the victim had a choice: if he deliberately uses the obstructed part, his own act is the effective cause; if the entire road is blocked, the obstructor is liable due to compulsion (idtirar).

Liability for Sprinkling with Permission: The Role of Istihsan
Ruling on liability with istihsan for sprinkling with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when water is sprinkled with the owner's permission in his courtyard, and explain why the liability transfers to the orderer by istihsan.

Core Idea
The one who orders, not the one who sprinkles, bears liability by istihsan.

In Hanafi fiqh, liability for harm caused by an action generally falls on the direct actor. However, when the action is performed on the owner's property with his permission, the owner becomes liable. This lesson examines a key ruling from al-Hidayah that illustrates this exception through the principle of istihsan (juristic preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
What is the action? (sprinkling water) Where? (in the courtyard, fina', of a shop) Who acts? (the sprinkler) Who gives permission? (the shop owner)
2
Apply the general rule of liability
Under qiyas, the direct actor (sprinkler) would be liable for harm caused. State why this would be the baseline.
Qiyas would place daman on the fāʿil (doer).
3
Recognize the departure by istihsan
The text states that by istihsan, liability shifts to al-amir (the one who ordered). Understand that istihsan allows departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
Istihsan here is based on the owner's control and authorization.
4
Derive the conditions for the ruling
What conditions make this transfer valid? (1) The area is the owner's fina', (2) the sprinkling is done with explicit permission, (3) the harm occurs due to the action.)
5
Contrast with the opposite view
Note that other schools may hold the sprinkler liable. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د کان کی فناء میں مالک دکان کی اجازت سے پانی چھڑکا اور کوئی چیز ہلاک ہوگئی تو استحسانا ضمان آمر پر ہوگا
ولورش فناء حانوت بإذن صاحبه فضـمـان مـا عـطـب عـلـى الآمر استحسانا
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے دکان کی فناء میں مالک دکان کی اجازت سے پانی چھڑ کا تو جو چیز وہاں ہلاک ہوگی استحسانا اس کا منعمان آمر پر ہوگا۔ تشریح زید نے قہ کو حکم دیا کہ اس کی دکان کے سامنے سڑک پر نہیں بلکہ اس کی فناء میں پانی چھڑک دے اس نے چھڑک دیا تو اگر وہاں کوئی پھسل کر مر جائے تو سقہ اس کا ضامن نہ ہو گا بلکہ اس کا ضامن صاحب دکان ہوگا۔
And if he sprinkles water in the courtyard of a shop with the owner's permission, then the liability for what is destroyed is on the one who ordered (al-amin) by istihsan. Translation: And if he sprinkled in the courtyard of the shop with the owner's permission, then whatever is destroyed there, by istihsan its compensation is on the one who ordered. Explanation: Zaid ordered Qah to sprinkle water not on the road but in the courtyard of his shop; he did so. If someone slips and dies, then Qah is not liable; rather the owner of the shop is liable.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability when water is sprinkled in a private courtyard (fina') of a shop with the owner's permission. The principle is that the one who gave the order (al-amin) bears the liability, not the actual sprinkler. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference), because the owner has control and authorization. The Urdu commentary gives an example: if Zaid orders Khalid to sprinkle water in his courtyard, and someone dies from slipping, Zaid (the owner) is liable, not Khalid. This is an exception to the general rule that the direct actor is liable; here the orderer is deemed responsible due to his authority.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The open courtyard or area in front of a shop or house, often used for business purposes.
آمر (amir): The person who orders or authorizes an action, in this case the shop owner who permits sprinkling.
استحسانا (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of legal reasoning where the jurist departs from analogy (qiyas) for a stronger conflicting evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of sprinkling water in the courtyard with the owner's permission, who is liable if someone slips?
A) The person who sprinkled the water.
B) The owner who gave permission.
C) Both are equally liable.
D) No one, because it was an accident.

Key Takeaway
When water is sprinkled with the owner's permission in his courtyard, the owner is liable by istihsan, not the sprinkler.

Liability for Building in Private Courtyard vs. Public Road
Ruling on liability for building in courtyard vs. middle of road

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of liability when a hired worker builds on private versus public property, distinguishing between valid and invalid commands.

Core Idea
Liability follows the validity of the command: a valid order makes the orderer liable; an invalid order makes the worker liable.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle in tort liability (diyat). When a hired worker builds a structure on someone's order, who bears responsibility if someone dies? The answer depends on whether the order itself was valid or invalid. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to assign liability to the orderer when the command is lawful, and to the worker when the command is unlawful. We'll explore the ruling, its proof, and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
The passage presents two cases: building in the private courtyard (fina') of a shop, and building in the middle of the road. Identify who is liable in each.
First scenario: orderer liable. Second: worker liable.
2
Understand the proof: istihsan
The ruling for the private courtyard is given 'by istihsan'. Understand that istihsan is a rational preference over qiyas. Here, the validity of the command makes the orderer the principal, not the worker.
Istihsan overrides the default qiyas that the direct actor (worker) is liable.
3
Analyze the reason for the second ruling
The worker is liable in the public road case 'due to the invalidity of the order' (li-fasad al-amr). The command is invalid because building on public road is unlawful. The worker knows this, so he becomes a transgressor.
Invalidity transfers liability to the worker.
4
Compare with the opposing school's reasoning
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may argue that the direct actor is always liable. The Hanafi response distinguishes: a valid command makes the worker an instrument; an invalid command makes him an independent agent.
This shows the importance of the command's validity in Hanafi jurisprudence.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The ikhtilaf results in different liability assignments in real cases. In Hanafi, if the order is valid, the orderer pays blood money; in Shafi'i, the worker might pay.
The tarjih (preference) in Hidayah is for the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزدور سے دکان کے سامنے چھجہ بنانے کا کہا پھر کوئی پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان آمر پر ہوگا
وإذا استاجر أجيرا ليبنى له فى فناء حانوته فتعقل به إنسان بعد فراغه من العمل فمات يجب الضمان على الآمر استحسانا ولو كان أمره بالبناء فى وسط الطريق فالضمان على الأجير لفساد الأمر
ترجمہ اور جب کہ کسی اجیر کو اجرت پر طے کیا تا کہ اس کی دکان کی فناء میں اس کے لئے عمارت بنائے پس اس کے عمل سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد اس سے کوئی انسان پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان استحسانا آمر پر واجب ہوگا اور اگر اس کو حکم دیا ہوراستہ کے بیچ میں عمارت بنانے کا تو حکم کے فساد کی وجہ سے ضمان اجیر پر ہوگا۔ تشریح زید نے خالد سے کہا کہ میری دکان کے سامنے مثلاً چھجہ بنادے اس نے بنا دیا جب وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا اب کوئی اس میں پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان زید پر ہو گا۔ اور اگر زید نے خالد سے کہا کہ سڑک کے بیچ میں ایک کمرہ بنا دے اور خالد نے بنا دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی مرگیا تو یہاں خالد پر ضمان ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں حکم درست ہے اور دوسری صورت میں حکم درست نہیں بلکہ فاسد ہے کیونکہ خالد کو یہ تو علم ہو گا کہ سڑک کے بیچ میں مکان نہیں بنایا جاتا۔
And if he hires a worker to build for him in the courtyard of his shop, and a person slips on it after the work is finished and dies, the liability is on the one who ordered (al-amin) by istihsan. But if he ordered him to build in the middle of the road, the liability is on the worker due to the invalidity of the order. Translation: Explanation: Zaid told Khalid to build a canopy in front of his shop; he built it. After completion, someone slips and dies; liability is on Zaid. But if Zaid told Khalid to build a room in the middle of the road and he did, and someone collides and dies, then liability is on Khalid because in the first case the order is valid, but in the second case it is invalid because Khalid knows that one does not build in the middle of the road.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability when a hired worker is ordered to build a structure. Two scenarios: (1) If the worker builds on the shop owner's private courtyard (fina'), and after completion someone dies from slipping on it, the liability is on the one who gave the order (the shop owner) by istihsan. (2) If the worker is ordered to build in the middle of the public road, and someone dies, the liability is on the worker himself. The reasoning is that ordering construction on a private property is valid, so the orderer is liable as the principal. Conversely, ordering construction on a public road is invalid (fasid) because it is inherently unlawful; the worker should know this, so he bears liability for his own transgression. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that liability follows the validity of the command.

Key Terms
أجير (ajir): A hired worker, specifically one hired to perform a specific task like building.
فساد الأمر (fasad al-amr): Invalidity of the command because the commanded act is inherently unlawful (e.g., building on public road).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a worker to build a canopy in his private courtyard. After completion, a person slips on it and dies. Who is liable?
A) The worker, because he built it.
B) The man who hired him, because the order was valid.
C) Both equally.
D) No one.

Key Takeaway
The orderer is liable for a lawful command; the worker is liable for an unlawful command because the validity of the command determines who bears responsibility for harm.

Liability for Digging a Well or Placing a Stone in the Road
Ruling on liability with proof and qiyas extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for harm caused by digging a well or placing a stone in a public road, and explain why the 'aqila bears responsibility for human life but not for property.

Core Idea
For a human, diyah is on the 'aqila; for an animal, the perpetrator pays from his own wealth.

The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling when someone creates a hazard on a public road. The key distinction is based on the type of victim: human or animal. This lesson unpacks the ruling from al-Quduri's matn and explains the rationale behind the different payors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
Recognize that digging a well or placing a stone on a public road without permission is an act of transgression (ta'addi). This triggers liability for any harm caused.
The act is defined by the public nature of the road and lack of permission.
2
Determine the victim type
The ruling distinguishes between a human (insan) and an animal (bahima). The payor changes based on this distinction.
Human = diyah on 'aqila; Animal = daman on individual.
3
Understand the role of the 'aqila
The 'aqila (tribe) is responsible for blood money (diyah) for human life only, not for property. This is a social solidarity mechanism.
The 'aqila shares the burden only for human life (nafs).
4
Apply the qiyas to similar acts
The ruling is extended to throwing dirt or making mud on the road, as they share the same effective cause (illa): creating a hazard through transgression.
Qiyas is based on the illa of ta'addi.
5
Formulate the complete ruling
Combine the elements: ta'addi + causation + human/animal victim = liability with respective payor.
No further conditions mentioned; the ruling is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیر مملوکہ زمین (یعنی راستہ میں کنواں کھدایا پتھر رکھ دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی انسان یا چوپایہ مر گیا ضمان واجب ہوگا
قال ومن حفرا بيرا في طريق المسلمين أو وضع حجرا فتلف بذالك إنسان فديته على عاقلته وإن تلفت بهيمة فضمانها في ماله لأنه متعد فيه فيضمن ما يتولد منه غير أن العاقلة تتحمل النفس دون المال فكان ضمان البهيمة فى ماله وإلقاء التراب واتخاذ الطين فى الطريق بمنزلة إلقاء الحجر والخشبة لما ذكرنا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کنواں کھودا مسلمانوں کے راستہ میں یا پتھر رکھا پس اس کی وجہ سے کوئی انسان تلف ہو گیا تو اس کی دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی۔ اور اگر کوئی چوپایہ ہلاک ہوا تو اس کا ضمان اس کے مال میں ہوگا اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے تو جو چیز اس سے پیدا ہوگی وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا مگر برادری نفس کا حمل کرتی ہے نہ کہ مال کا تو چوپائے کا ضمان اس کے مال میں ہوگا اور راستہ میں مٹی ڈالنایا گارا بنانا پھر او لکڑی ڈالنے کے مثل ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مملوکہ زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہو یا پھر رکھ دیا ہو جس میں کوئی انسان یا کوئی چوپایہ گر کر یا ٹکرا کر مر گیا۔ تو دونوں صورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ اس کی زیادتی ہے کہ اس نے راستہ میں یہ حرکت کی ہے۔ لیکن آدمی کی دیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی اور چوپایہ کا ضمان خود اس شخص پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ برادری مال کا تحمل نہیں کرتی صرف نفس کا کرتی ہے۔
And whoever digs a well in the path of the Muslims or places a stone, and by that a person dies, his blood money is on his 'aqila (tribe); and if an animal is destroyed, its compensation is from his own wealth, because he is transgressor (muta'addi), so he is liable for what results from it, except that the 'aqila bears responsibility for human life not for wealth. Thus the compensation for the animal is from his own wealth. And throwing dirt or making mud on the road is analogous to throwing a stone or wood for the reason we mentioned. Explanation: If someone digs a well or places a stone in his non-owned land (i.e., the road), and a human or animal dies by falling or colliding, then liability is wajib in both cases because it is his transgression. But the blood money for a human is on the 'aqila, while for an animal it is on his own wealth, because the tribe does not bear liability for wealth, only for life.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability for digging a well or placing a stone in a public road. The author (al-Quduri) states: (1) If a person dies as a result, the blood money (diyah) is payable by the 'aqila (the perpetrator's tribe or group). (2) If an animal is killed, the compensation is from the perpetrator's own personal wealth. The reason given is that the perpetrator is a transgressor (muta'addi) and is liable for all resulting harm. However, the 'aqila only bears liability for human life (nafs), not for property (mal). Therefore, animal compensation falls on the individual. The rule extends to throwing dirt or making mud on the road, analogous to placing stones or wood. The Urdu commentary confirms that both cases (human and animal) entail liability, but the payor differs. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of diyah: the 'aqila shares the burden for human life to provide social solidarity, but property losses remain the individual's responsibility.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('aqila): The male relatives (tribe) of the perpetrator who are responsible for paying blood money (diyah) for unintentional homicide.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for unlawful homicide or bodily harm.
متعد (muta'addi): One who transgresses by acting without right, causing harm; here, digging in a public road without permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man digs a well on a public road and a donkey falls and dies, from whose wealth is compensation paid?
A) The 'aqila of the man.
B) The man's own personal wealth.
C) The government treasury.
D) No compensation is due.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between human and animal harm in public road hazards: the 'aqila bears diyah for human life, while the perpetrator personally compensates for animal losses.

Liability for Canopy Worker: Employer vs. Worker based on Location
Analyses liability for death caused by completed construction, distinguishing by location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a construction worker's completed work causes a death, and distinguish when liability falls on the employer (by istihsan) versus on the worker (due to invalid order).

Core Idea
The employer bears liability for construction in his own courtyard; the worker bears it if the order was unlawful.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding liability (daman) when a hired worker builds a structure and later someone dies from slipping on it. The key distinction is based on the location of the construction: if built in the employer's fina' (courtyard), the employer is liable by istihsan; if built in the middle of a public road, the worker is liable because the order itself is invalid. Understanding this distinction requires appreciating the Hanafi principle of istihsan and the concept of a valid versus invalid command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: building in the fina' (courtyard) of the shop and building in the middle of a public road.
2
Note the ruling for each
In the fina', liability is on the employer (aamir); in the middle of the road, liability is on the worker (ajir).
The term 'liability' here refers to the obligation to pay blood money (diyya) for the death.
3
Understand the legal basis
For the fina' case, the ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). For the road case, it is because the order itself is legally invalid (fasid) – constructing in the public way is unlawful.
Istihsan overrides the qiyas that would hold the worker liable in both cases.
4
Apply the reasoning to similar cases
When presented with a new scenario, first identify whether the construction is on the employer's private property (fina') or on public land. Then apply the corresponding liability rule.
The fina' includes any land legally considered part of the employer's premises, even if not enclosed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہاں کوئی پھسل کر مر جائے تو سقہ اس کا ضامن نہ ہو گا بلکہ اس کا ضامن صاحب دکان ہوگا۔ مزدور سے دکان کے سامنے چھجہ بنانے کا کہا پھر کوئی پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان آمر پر ہوگا و إذا استاجر أجيرا ليبنى له فى فناء حانوته فتعقل به إنسان بعد فراغه من العمل فمات يجب الضمان على الآمر استحسانا ولو كان أمره بالبناء فى وسط الطريق فالضمان على الأجير لفساد الأمر ترجمہ اور جب کہ کسی اجیر کو اجرت پر طے کیا تا کہ اس کی دکان کی فناء میں اس کے لئے عمارت بنائے پس اس کے عمل سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد اس سے کوئی انسان پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان استحسانا آمر پر واجب ہوگا اور اگر اس کو حکم دیا ہوراستہ کے بیچ میں عمارت بنانے کا تو حکم کے فساد کی وجہ سے ضمان اجیر پر ہوگا۔ تشریح زید نے خالد سے کہا کہ میری دکان کے سامنے مثلاً چھجہ بنادے اس نے بنا دیا جب وہ کام سے فارغ ہو گیا اب کوئی اس میں پھسل کر مر گیا تو ضمان زید پر ہو گا۔ اور اگر زید نے خالد سے کہا کہ سڑک کے بیچ میں ایک کمرہ بنا دے اور خالد نے بنا دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی مرگیا تو یہاں خالد پر ضمان ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں حکم درست ہے اور دوسری صورت میں حکم درست نہیں بلکہ فاسد ہے کیونکہ خالد کو یہ تو علم ہو گا کہ سڑک کے بیچ میں مکان نہیں بنایا جاتا۔
And when he hires a worker to build for him in the courtyard of his shop, then a person slips on it after the worker finishes the work and dies, the guarantee is obligatory upon the employer by istihsan. And if he ordered him to build in the middle of the road, then the guarantee is upon the worker due to the corruption of the order.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on liability for harm caused by a construction after the worker has finished. It distinguishes between two scenarios: if the building is in the shop's courtyard (fina'), the employer is liable by istihsan; if in the middle of the public road, the worker is liable because the order itself is invalid (fasid) — building in the road is known to be unlawful. The commentary illustrates with Zayd and Khalid: if Zayd asks Khalid to build a canopy in front of the shop and someone later slips and dies, Zayd (the employer) pays the diyya. But if Zayd asks Khalid to build a room in the middle of the road, Khalid is liable because he should know better.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Preference of a ruling over a stronger analogy due to equity or custom; used here to shift liability to employer.
فناء (fina'): Courtyard or forecourt of a house/shop; considered private property in Hanafi law.
ضمان (daman): Liability, guarantee, or obligation to compensate; here refers to paying blood money for death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zayd hires Khalid to build a canopy in the courtyard of his shop, and a person later dies by slipping on it, who is liable?
A) Khalid, because he built it
B) Zayd, because the order was in his own courtyard
C) No one, because it was an accident
D) The state, because it is a public road

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the location of construction determines liability: employer pays if built on his property (by istihsan), worker pays if built on public property (order invalid).

Liability for Digging a Well or Placing a Stone in a Public Road
States liability for human and animal death from road obstructions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for creating an obstruction in a public road and explain why the diyya for human death falls on the aqila while compensation for animal death falls on the offender's own wealth.

Core Idea
The aqila bears blood money for human life but not for property; thus, animal compensation is from the offender's wealth.

This lesson from al-Quduri's matn clarifies the liability when someone creates a hazard in a public road. The ruling distinguishes between human and animal victims based on the scope of the aqila's responsibility. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the principle that the aqila's duty is limited to human life (nafs), not property (mal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The act of digging a well or placing a stone in a public road is an act of transgression (ta'addi) because it endangers others. The ruling also covers throwing dirt or making mud.
Ta'addi is a key concept: any act that exceeds proper limits and causes harm triggers liability.
2
State the basic ruling for human death
If a human dies as a direct result, the diyya (blood money) is payable by the aqila (the offender's clan or male relatives).
Diyya is wajib, but the payer is not the offender himself.
3
State the basic ruling for animal death
If an animal dies, the compensation (guarantee) is paid from the offender's own wealth, not by the aqila.
The text uses 'fi malihi' meaning his own property.
4
Explain the rationale
The aqila traditionally bears responsibility for unintentional killing of humans, but not for property damage. The aqila's liability is limited to human life (nafs); property damage is the offender's personal responsibility.
This is a custom-based rule recognized in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Extend the ruling to similar acts
The same ruling applies to throwing dirt, making mud, or placing wood in the road, as these are analogous obstructions (like placing a stone or digging a well).
The faqih uses qiyas to extend the ruling.

Source Text

غير مملوکہ زمین (یعنی راستہ میں کنواں کھدایا پتھر رکھ دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی انسان یا چوپایہ مر گیا ضمان واجب ہوگا قال ومن حفرا بيرا في طريق المسلمين أو وضع حجرا فتلف بذالك إنسان فديته على عاقلته وإن تلفت بهيمة فضمانها في ماله لأنه متعد فيه فيضمن ما يتولد منه غير أن العاقلة تتحمل النفس دون المال فكان ضمان البهيمة فى ماله وإلقاء التراب واتخاذ الطين فى الطريق بمنزلة إلقاء الحجر والخشبة لما ذكرنا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کنواں کھودا مسلمانوں کے راستہ میں یا پتھر رکھا پس اس کی وجہ سے کوئی انسان تلف ہو گیا تو اس کی دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی۔ اور اگر کوئی چوپایہ ہلاک ہوا تو اس کا ضمان اس کے مال میں ہوگا اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں متعدی ہے تو جو چیز اس سے پیدا ہوگی وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا مگر برادری نفس کا حمل کرتی ہے نہ کہ مال کا تو چوپائے کا ضمان اس کے مال میں ہوگا اور راستہ میں مٹی ڈالنایا گارا بنانا پھر او لکڑی ڈالنے کے مثل ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مملوکہ زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہو یا پھر رکھ دیا ہو جس میں کوئی انسان یا کوئی چوپایہ گر کر یا ٹکرا کر مر گیا۔ تو دونوں صورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ اس کی زیادتی ہے کہ اس نے راستہ میں یہ حرکت کی ہے۔ لیکن آدمی کی دیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی اور چوپایہ کا ضمان خود اس شخص پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ برادری مال کا تحمل نہیں کرتی صرف نفس کا کرتی ہے۔
He said: And whoever digs a well in the path of the Muslims or places a stone, and a person is thus destroyed, his blood money is upon his aqila. And if an animal is destroyed, its guarantee is in his wealth because he is a transgressor, so he guarantees what results from it, except that the aqila bears the life (diya) and not the property, so the guarantee of the animal is in his wealth. And throwing dust and making mud in the road is like throwing a stone and a piece of wood due to what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri covers liability for creating obstructions in a public road. If a person digs a well or puts a stone, and a human dies, the diyya (blood money) is on the aqila (the offender's clan). If an animal dies, the compensation is from the offender's own property. The reason given is that the aqila bears only human life (nafs), not property. This is because the act is an aggression (ta'addi). The same ruling applies to throwing dirt or making mud in the road, as these are akin to placing a stone or wood. The commentary clarifies that in both cases (human or animal death) the guarantee is wajib, but the responsible party differs.

Key Terms
عاقلة (aqila): The clan or male relatives who bear the blood money for unintentional killing.
تعدي (ta'addi): Act of transgression or exceeding proper limits; here it refers to creating hazard in public road.
دية (diya): Blood money paid for killing a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both on the offender's own wealth
D) No liability because it is a public road

Key Takeaway
The aqila bears blood money for human life but not for property; thus, compensation for animal death is from the offender's own wealth.

Liability for Sweeping vs. Gathering Garbage in Public Road
Contrasts liability for sweeping vs. gathering garbage on public road.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sweeping and gathering garbage on a public road in terms of liability, and state the Hanafi ruling based on the concept of ta'addi.

Core Idea
Liability in public road acts depends on whether the act is transgression (ta'addi) or removal of harm.

The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between two seemingly similar activities on a public road: sweeping and gathering rubbish. Both involve the road, but one is commendable and the other is a transgression. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind the difference, focusing on the key concept of ta'addi (aggression) that determines liability for harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: sweeping the road and gathering rubbish on the road. State each clearly.
2
Determine the ruling for each
Note that the sweeper is not liable, while the gatherer is liable. This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Find the legal basis (ta'addi)
The key distinction is the presence or absence of ta'addi. The sweeper did not commit ta'addi, the gatherer did.
Ta'addi means transgression, an act exceeding what is permitted.
4
Explain the reasoning (talil)
Sweeping removes harm from the road, so it is not an aggression. Gathering creates an obstruction, which is a transgression. The intent and nature of the act are decisive.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a person who digs a trench to drain water by the roadside. Is this analogous to sweeping or gathering? Use the ta'addi criterion.
If the trench is a hazard, it may be gathering; if it improves safety, it may be like sweeping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راستہ صاف کیا وہاں خالد پھسل کر گر گیا اور مر گیا تو ضامن نہ ہوگا اور کوڑا کرکٹ راستہ میں جمع کر دیا تو ضامن ہوگا بخلاف ما إذا كنس الطريق فعطب بموضع كنسه إنسان حيث لم يضمن لأنه ليس بمتعد فإنه ما أحدث شيئا فيه إما قصد دفع الأذى عن الطريق حتى لو جمع الكناسة فى الطريق وتعقل به إنسان كان ضامنا لتعديه بشغله ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے راستہ صاف کیا پس اس کے صاف کرنے کی جگہ میں کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا تو وہ ضامن نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ متعدی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اس (راستہ میں کچھ بنایا نہیں اس نے راستہ سے تکلیف دہ چیز کو دور کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے کوڑا راستہ میں جمع کیا اور اس میں کوئی آدمی پھسل گیا تو وہ ضامن ہو گا۔ اس کے متعدی ہونے کی وجہ سے راستہ کو مشغول کرنے کی وجہ ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے راستہ صاف کیا تو یہ جرم نہیں بلکہ عبادت ہے لیکن جہاں سے اس نے صاف کیا وہاں خالد پھسل کر گر گیا اور مرگیا تو زید ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر کوڑا کرکٹ راستہ میں جمع کر دیا تو ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اس کو راستہ میں ڈالنا تعدی ہے لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔
Contrary to when he sweeps the road, then a person trips at the place he swept and dies, he is not liable because he is not a transgressor, for he did not create anything in it; rather he intended to remove harm from the road. Even so, if he gathers the rubbish in the road and a person trips on it, he is liable due to his transgression by occupying the road.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two acts on the road. Sweeping (kans) is a commendable act of removing harm, so if someone slips on the swept area and dies, the sweeper is not liable because he did not commit an aggression (ta'addi). However, if he gathers rubbish (qumama) in the road, that is an aggression because he is occupying the road with an obstruction, so he is liable if someone dies. The commentary emphasizes that sweeping is like worship, while gathering garbage is transgression.

Key Terms
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; an act causing harm beyond what is allowed.
كنس (kans): Sweeping; an act of cleaning the road.
كناسة (kunasa): Garbage or rubbish swept from the road.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zayd sweeps the road and someone later slips and dies on the swept area, is Zayd liable?
A) Yes, because sweeping can make the road slippery
B) No, because sweeping is not an aggression
C) Yes, if he sweeps during the night
D) No, because the victim was negligent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts that remove harm (no liability) and acts that create harm (liability), based on the presence of transgression (ta'addi).

Liability When a Stone is Moved to Another Spot
Determines liability when a stone placed by one person is moved by another, causing harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine liability in a case where one person places an obstruction and another moves it, causing harm, applying the Hanafi principle of annulment (naskh) of the original act.

Core Idea
Liability transfers to the mover because the original act is annulled when the obstruction is removed.

Imagine someone places a stone in a public road, and another person comes along and moves it to a different spot. If a third person then trips on that stone and dies, who is responsible? This lesson from al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling: the mover is liable, not the original placer. The key insight is that the first act is legally 'annulled' once the obstruction is removed, making the mover's act the direct cause of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the scenario: Zayd places a stone, Khalid moves it to another spot, and Bakr trips on the moved stone and dies. The ruling is that Khalid (the mover) is liable for the death (daman wajib).
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reason given is that Zayd's act is 'annulled' (mansukh) because the spot he occupied is now empty. His act no longer has legal effect. Khalid's act creates a new obstruction at a different spot, so he is the direct cause.
The term 'naskh' is borrowed from usul al-fiqh meaning abrogation, but here it means nullification of the prior act's effect.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The logic: once a harmful object is removed, the original placement ceases to be a legal cause. The new placement becomes the only remaining cause. This is an example of attributing liability to the most proximate and operative act.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may hold both parties liable or the original placer. The Hanafi position is that the mover alone is liable because his act is a new aggression (fi'l mubtadi').
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi view is based on the principle that the first act is fully nullified.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position from zahir al-riwayah is that the mover is liable. This ruling is clear and based on the direct causal link.
No tarjih authority is explicitly cited in this passage, but al-Hidayah presents it as the established view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے راستہ میں پتھر رکھا دوسرے نے دوسری جگہ پر رکھ دیا، ایک شخص الجھ کر مر گیا تو ضمان کس پر ہے و لو وضع حجرا فنحاه غيره عن موضعه فعطب به إنسان فالضمان على الذى نحاه لأن حكم فعله قد انتسخ لفراغ ما شغله وإنما اشتغل بالفعل الثاني موضع آخر ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے (راستہ میں پتھر رکھا پس اس کو غیر نے راستہ سے ہٹا دیا۔ پس اس کی وجہ سے کوئی انسان ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضمان اس شخص پر ہو گا جس نے اس کو دور کیا ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا ( واضع اول) فعل منسوخ ہو گیا ہے اس راستہ کے خالی ہو جانے کی وجہ سے جس کو اس نے مشغول کیا تھا اور دوسرے سے فعل سے دوسری جگہ مشغول ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح زید نے راستہ میں کوئی پتھر رکھ دیا خالد نے اس کو اس جگہ سے ہٹا کر دوسری جگہ راستہ ہی میں رکھ دیا۔ اب بکر اس میں الجھ کر مر گیا تو منمان خالد پر ہو گا۔ زید پر نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ یہاں دو فعل میں ایک زید کا اور دوسرا خالد کا ، خالد کے فعل سے زید کا فعل منسوخ ہو گیا ، کیونکہ زید کے فعل سے راستہ کو جو حصہ مشغول ہوا تھا اب وہ راستہ خالی ہو چکا ہے، لہذا اس کا نفعل ندارد ہو گیا ، البتہ خالد کے فعل سے راستہ کا دوسراحصہ مشغول تھا جس کی وجہ سے بکر مرا ہے تو ضمان خالد پر واجب ہوگا۔
And if he places a stone, then another removes it from its place, and a person is injured by it, the guarantee is upon the one who removed it because the effect of his (the first's) action is annulled due to the emptying of what he occupied, and the second action occupies another place.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where one person (Zayd) places a stone in the road, and another (Khalid) moves it to a different spot in the same road. If someone later trips on the stone and dies, the liability is on Khalid, not Zayd. The reason is that Zayd's original act of placing the stone is annulled (mansukh) once the stone is removed; the obstruction he created is gone. Khalid's act of moving it creates a new obstruction at a different spot, and since the harm came from that new spot, he is liable. The commentary illustrates with Zayd, Khalid, and Bakr.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansukh): Annulled; the legal effect of the first action is terminated.
فعل (fi'l): Action; in this context, the physical act of placing or moving the stone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zayd, because he originally placed the stone
B) Both Zayd and Khalid equally
C) Khalid, because his act created the new obstruction
D) No one, because the stone was moved

Key Takeaway
The mover bears liability because the original obstruction is annulled upon removal.

Digging a Pit in the Road: Sultan's Permission and Liability
Fragment from al-Jami' al-Saghir on liability for digging a pit with sultan's order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the sultan's order may remove liability for digging a pit in a public road, and identify the key factor from the incomplete text.

Core Idea
The sultan's permission can shield a digger from liability, but the full ruling is incomplete.

This lesson examines a fragment from al-Jami' al-Saghir concerning digging a pit (balu'a) in a public road. The text introduces the sultan's order or compulsion as a factor, but is cut off. We will analyze what is known from Hanafi law and the significance of the missing conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the legal issue
Recognize that digging a pit in a public road (balu'a) is a potentially harmful act. In Hanafi fiqh, unauthorized acts that cause damage lead to liability (daman).
This falls under the chapter of diyat (injuries) or ghurrah (compensation).
2
Recognize the factor mentioned
The fragment states 'if the sultan orders him to do so or compels him'. This indicates that the sultan's authority is a key variable that may affect liability.
The sultan represents the state; his order may transfer liability from the individual to the state.
3
Recall the general Hanafi rule without permission
Without sultan's permission, digging a pit in a public road is a transgression (ta'di). If someone falls and is harmed, the digger is liable for damages.
This is based on the hadith: 'Whoever digs a pit, he is responsible for its consequences.'
4
Consider the incomplete text and possible complete ruling
The text cuts off after 'lam' (not). A likely completion: 'lam yadman' (he is not liable). Thus, with sultan's order, the digger may be exempt from liability because he acted under lawful authority.
The mufta bihi position in later Hanafi works supports this: the sultan's order for public benefit removes individual liability.

And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: concerning a pit that a man digs in the road: if the sultan orders him to do so or compels him to do it, not...

This is a fragment from al-Jami' al-Saghir about digging a balu'a (cesspit or pit) in the public road. It begins the ruling: if the sultan orders or forces the digging, then... but the text is cut off. The complete ruling would address whether the digger is liable or the state. Without the full text, we cannot state the complete ruling.

سلطان (sultan): Ruler or authority who can grant permission for such acts.

Liability for Digging in the Road: With and Without Ruler's Permission
Explains liability for digging a balu'ah in the road depending on ruler's permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for digging a balu'ah in a public road and explain why permission from the ruler removes liability.

Core Idea
Permission from the ruler transforms the act from transgression to authorized use, removing liability.

When someone digs a hole in a public road, the legal consequences depend critically on whether the ruler authorized the act. This lesson explores the Hanafi position from al-Jami' al-Saghir, clarifying the concept of ta'addi (transgression) and the authority of the sultan over public rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Two Scenarios
The passage discusses a man digging a balu'ah (hole/drain) in a public road. There are two scenarios: with the ruler's permission (command or compulsion) and without it.
2
State the Ruling for Each Scenario
With permission: no liability (ghayr damin). Without permission: liable (damin).
3
Understand the Rationale: Ta'addi
The key concept is ta'addi (transgression). With permission, the act is not ta'addi because the ruler has wilayah over public rights. Without permission, it becomes ta'addi for three reasons: interfering in others' rights, overriding the imam's opinion, and violating the condition of safety inherent in the permission to use the road.
4
Generalize the Ruling
The same detail applies to all actions in the public road because the underlying meaning (ma'na) is the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الجامع الصغير فى البالوعة يحفرها الرجل فى الطريق فإن أمره السلطان بذالك أو أجبره عليه لم يضمن لأنه غير متعد حيث فعل ما فعل بأمر من له الولاية فى حقوق العامة وإن كان بغير أمره فهو متعد إما بالتصرف فى حق غيره أو بالافتيات على رأى الإمام أو هو مباح مقيد بشرط السلامة وكذا الجواب على هذا التفصيل في جميع ما فعل في طريق العامة مما ذكرناه وغيره لأن المعنى لا يختلف
ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے اس بچہ کے بارے میں جس کو مرد راستے میں کھودنے پس اگر اس کو بادشاہ نے اس کا حکم کیا ہو یا اس کو مجبور کیا ہوتو اس پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ غیر متعدی ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے جو کچھ کیا ہے اس شخص کے حکم سے کیا ہے جس کو حقوق عامہ میں ولایت ہے اور اگر اس کے حکم کے بغیر ہو تو وہ متعدی ہے یا تو اپنے غیر کے حق میں تصرف کی وجہ سے یا امام کی رائے پر پیش قدمی کرنے کی وجہ سے یا اس لئے کہ یہ مباح کام تھا جو سلامتی کی شرط کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور ایسے ہی جواب ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق ان تمام کاموں میں جو اس نے عام لوگوں کے راستہ میں کئے ان کاموں میں سے جن کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور اس کے غیر میں سے اس لئے کہ معنی مختلف نہ ہوں گے۔
تشریح کسی شخص نے راستہ میں جو تصرف امام کی اجازت یا امام کے حکم سے کیا ہو اور اس میں کوئی الجھ کر مر جائے تو اس کے متعدی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر امام کی اجازت کے بغیر کرے گا تو ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اب وہ متعدی ہے، اور متعدی ہونے کی تین وجہ ہیں۔
-1 دوسروں کے حق میں تصرف کرنے کی وجہ سے۔
-2 امام کی رائے پر پیش قدمی کرنے کی وجہ سے۔

And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: regarding a hole (balu'ah) that a man digs in the road: if the ruler orders him to do so or compels him, he is not liable because he is not a transgressor, as he acted by the command of one who has authority over public rights. But if it was without his command, he is a transgressor, either by acting in the right of others, or by encroaching upon the opinion of the imam, or it is permissible restricted by the condition of safety. And similarly the answer according to this detail applies to all actions done in the public road of what we have mentioned and other matters, because the meaning does not differ.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir (a Zahir al-Riwayah text) discusses liability for digging a balu'ah (hole/drain) in a public road. If the ruler (sultan) has authorized or compelled the digging, there is no liability because the person is not a transgressor; the ruler has authority over public rights. Without the ruler's permission, the person is a transgressor for three reasons: (1) interfering in the rights of others, (2) overriding the imam's authority, (3) because a permitted act is conditioned on safety. The Urdu commentary adds that if the hole causes someone's death, liability applies only if done without permission. The 'tanbih' explains that balu'ah means a hole in the wall for drainage, and gives local examples like a 'kundi' or 'kheel' (water tank) and 'tanka' (well-like pit).

Key Terms
بالوعة (balu'ah): A hole or drain dug in the road for water drainage, often a small pit.
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or authority who has jurisdiction over public rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Permission from the ruler (sultan) removes liability for digging in public roads because the act is then done by one with authority over public rights.

Liability for Digging a Well in Own Property vs. Shared Courtyard
States ruling on liability for digging a well in one's own property or fina'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on liability (daman) for digging a well in one's own property versus a shared or public fina', and identify the condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
Ownership removes transgression; a shared fina' requires consent or the digger is liable.

This lesson examines when a person is liable for digging a well that causes harm to others. The key factor is the legal status of the land: if it is owned or under exclusive right, there is no liability; but if it is shared or communal, the digger is a transgressor and must compensate. The passage also notes a difference of opinion (qila) within the Hanafi school, which is resolved by affirming the final position as sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the locus of digging
Determine whether the person dug in his own property (milk), in the fina' (courtyard) of his house, or in a shared/public space.
The fina' can be owned or shared depending on context.
2
Assess ownership or right of use
If the fina' is owned by the digger or if he has a right to dig there (e.g., private courtyard), he is not a transgressor because he acts within his domain.
3
Apply the default rule
In owned property or private fina', no liability. If the fina' belongs to the community or is shared (like a dead-end alley), the digger is a causal agent (musabbib) and a transgressor, hence liable.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The phrase 'qila' indicates a difference: some Hanafi scholars say liability only applies if the fina' is not owned. The text affirms the latter view as correct (sahih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر اپنے ملک یا گھر کے فناء میں کنواں کھودا ضامن نہ ہوگا
وإن حفر في ملكه لم يضمن لأنه غير متعد وكذا إذا حفر فى فناء داره لأن له ذالك لمصلحة داره والفناء فى تصرفه وقيل هذا إذا كان الفناء مملوكا له أو كان له حق الجفر فيه لأنه غير متعد أما إذا كان لجماعة المسلمين أو مشتركا بأن كان في سكة غير نافذة فإنه يضمنه لأنه مسبب متعد وهذا صحيح
And similarly if he digs in his property, he is not liable because he is not a transgressor. And likewise if he digs in the courtyard (fina') of his house, because he has that right for the benefit of his house, and the courtyard is under his disposal. It is said: this is if the courtyard is owned by him or he has the right to dig in it because he is not a transgressor. But if it belongs to the community of Muslims or is shared, such as in a dead-end alley (sikka ghayr nafidha), then he is liable because he is a causal agent and transgressor, and this is correct.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on liability for digging wells. If one digs in his own property (milk) or in the fina' (courtyard or front area) of his house that is privately owned, there is no liability because he is not a transgressor. The fina' is under his control. However, if the fina' is communal property, such as in a dead-end alley shared by multiple residents, then digging there without collective consent makes him liable because he is a transgressor (mut'addi) and a causal agent (musabbib). The Urdu heading summarizes: no liability if in one's own property or fina'.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The courtyard or open area adjacent to a house, which is under the owner's use but may be shared in some cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the well is more than 10 cubits deep.
B) If the fina' is shared or belongs to the community.
C) Always, because any well is dangerous.
D) Never, because the fina' is under his disposal.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on liability for digging a well depends on ownership of the land: no liability in own property or private fina', but liability in shared or public spaces.

Liability for Digging in Public Way: Authority and Transgression
Ruling with proof on liability for digging in a public way

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for acts in a public way and explain the three reasons for transgression.

Core Idea
Ruler's order removes transgression; without it, the digger is liable.

This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir establishes a key principle in Hanafi tort law: the ruler's authority (wilāyah) over public rights can render a harmful act non-transgressive, thus removing liability. We will explore the ruling, the concept of transgression (ta'addī), and its threefold reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two scenarios
The act is digging in a public way. Two scenarios: with ruler's order (or compulsion) and without. Determine the ruling for each.
The child in the example is a minor, but the ruling applies to any person.
2
Understand the concept of transgression (ta'addī)
Without order, the digger is a muta'addī (transgressor). The text gives three reasons: acting in another's right, overruling the imam's opinion, and breaching the safety condition of a permissible act.
These reasons are not mutually exclusive; any one suffices for liability.
3
Apply the reasoning to other actions in the public way
The ruling extends to all acts in the public way, such as digging a water pit (balū'ah) or placing an object. The same logic applies: permission from authority negates transgression.
The principle is 'al-ma'nā lā yakhtalif' (the meaning does not differ).
4
Consider the modern application
Today, the ruler's authority is exercised by municipalities or government bodies. A permit is equivalent to the imam's order; without it, any harmful construction is transgressive.
This highlights the importance of official permission for public works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يضمن لأنه غير متعد حيث فعل ما فعل بأمر من له الولاية فى حقوق العامة وإن كان بغير أمره فهو متعد إما بالتصرف فى حق غيره أو بالافتيات على رأى الإمام أو هو مباح مقيد بشرط السلامة وكذا الجواب على هذا التفصيل في جميع ما فعل في طريق العامة مما ذكرناه وغيره لأن المعنى لا يختلف ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے اس بچہ کے بارے میں جس کو مرد راستے میں کھودنے پس اگر اس کو بادشاہ نے اس کا حکم کیا ہو یا اس کو مجبور کیا ہوتو اس پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ غیر متعدی ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے جو کچھ کیا ہے اس شخص کے حکم سے کیا ہے جس کو حقوق عامہ میں ولایت ہے اور اگر اس کے حکم کے بغیر ہو تو وہ متعدی ہے یا تو اپنے غیر کے حق میں تصرف کی وجہ سے یا امام کی رائے پر پیش قدمی کرنے کی وجہ سے یا اس لئے کہ یہ مباح کام تھا جو سلامتی کی شرط کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور ایسے ہی جواب ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق ان تمام کاموں میں جو اس نے عام لوگوں کے راستہ میں کئے ان کاموں میں سے جن کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور اس کے غیر میں سے اس لئے کہ معنی مختلف نہ ہوں گے۔ تشریح کسی شخص نے راستہ میں جو تصرف امام کی اجازت یا امام کے حکم سے کیا ہو اور اس میں کوئی الجھ کر مر جائے تو اس کے متعدی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر امام کی اجازت کے بغیر کرے گا تو ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اب وہ متعدی ہے، اور متعدی ہونے کی تین وجہ ہیں۔ -1 دوسروں کے حق میں تصرف کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ -۲ امام کی رائے پر پیش قدمی کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ مباح کام سلامتی کی شرط سے مقید ہوتا ہے تو راستہ سے انتقاع اگر چہ جائز ہے لیکن یہ شرط ہے کہ اس سے کسی کا نقصان نہ ہو اور یہاں نقصان ہو گیا اور جملہ تصرفات کا یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیہ بالوعة" کے معنی مودی کے ہیں یعنی دیوار میں ایسا سوراخ ہو جس میں اندر کا پانی نکل کر باہر آ جائے جس کا ترجمہ چہ بچہ سے کیا ہے، چہ بچہ اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں پانی آکر جمع ہو جائے۔ ہمارے علاقہ میں اب تو راج نہیں رہا ہمارے بچپنے میں رواج تھا کہ گھروں میں خصوصاً گھیروں میں پانی کا اسٹاک جمع کرنے کے لئے انتظام رکھتے تھے جس کو کنڈی یا کھیل کہتے ہیں تو اگر کسی نے وہی کھیل وغیرہ بنائی اور راستہ میں بنائی تو کیا حکم ہے؟ اور راجستھان کے علاقہ میں گھر میں کنویں جیسا ایک گڑھا بناتے ہیں جس کو تالاب سے پانی لا کر بھرتے رہتے ہیں اور اس میں سے ڈول سے کھینچ کر استعمال کرتے رہتے ہیں جس کو وہ ٹانکا کہتے ہیں اس پر بھی بالوعد کی تعریف صادق آئے گی ۔
He is liable because he is not transgressing since he did what he did by order of the one who has authority over public rights. And if it was without his order, then he is transgressing, either by acting in the right of another, or by overruling the imam's opinion, or because it is a permissible act conditional on safety. And similarly the answer according to this detail in everything done in the public way from what we mentioned and other than it, because the meaning does not differ. Translation: And in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is about a boy who dug in the road. If the king ordered him or compelled him, then there is no liability upon him because he is not transgressing; he did what he did by order of the one who has authority in public rights. But if without his order, then he is transgressing, either because of acting in another's right, or because of overstepping the imam's opinion, or because this permissible act was conditioned on safety. And the same answer applies to all actions in the public way, mentioned and unmentioned, because the meaning does not differ. Explanation: If a person acts in the road with the imam's permission or order and someone falls and dies, no liability due to non-transgression; but if without permission, he is liable as a transgressor. There are three reasons for being a transgressor: 1) acting in others' rights, 2) overruling the imam's opinion, 3) a permissible act conditioned on safety. Note: 'Balū'ah' means a hole in the wall for water draining, translated as 'cheh bacheh' (a water collecting pit). In our region it's now rare; in childhood, they used to make 'kundi' or 'kheel' for water storage. If someone makes such in the road, what is the ruling? In Rajasthan they make a well-like pit called 'tanka', filled with water from a tank; this also falls under balū'ah.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and talil (legal reasoning) on liability for digging in a public way. It opens by stating the principle: if a person (including a child) digs by order of the ruler who has authority (wilayah) over public matters, no liability (damān) arises because the act is not transgression (ghayr muta'addī). Without such order, the digger is a transgressor (muta'addī) and liable. The text provides three reasons for transgression: (1) acting in another's right (taṣarruf fī haqq ghayr), (2) overruling the imam's opinion (iftitā' 'alā ra'y al-imām), (3) a permissible act (mubāḥ) becomes conditional on safety, and here safety was breached. The ruling is from al-Jami' al-Saghir (Zahir al-Riwayah). The commentary then explains that the same ruling applies to all actions in the public way. Finally, a note clarifies the term 'balū'ah' (a water drainage hole) and its application, emphasising that any such construction in the road without permission incurs liability.

Key Terms
بالوعة (bālūʿah): A hole in a wall or ground for water drainage or collection, such as a pit for storing water.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation, especially blood money (diyah) if death results.
متعد (mutaʿaddī): A person who transgresses by performing an act without right, causing harm.
ولاية (wilāyah): Authority or jurisdiction, here over public rights (ḥuqūq ʿāmmah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, if a child digs a pit in a public road by order of the ruler, and someone falls and dies, is the child liable?
A) Yes, because the child caused the death.
B) No, because the act was ordered by the one with authority.
C) Yes, because the road is public property.
D) No, because a child is not legally responsible.

Key Takeaway
Liability in the public way hinges on authorization from the ruler; without it, any harmful act is transgression and requires compensation.

Liability for Digging a Well: Ownership and Transgression
Ruling on liability for digging a well in owned vs. shared courtyard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for digging a well in owned property, owned finā', and shared finā', and identify the condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
Transgression (ta'addī) determines liability; ownership or right negates transgression, but shared space makes one liable.

This lesson examines the conditions under which a person who digs a well becomes liable (ḍāmin) for any resulting harm. The key factor is whether the act is transgressive (muta'addī) or not. The Hanafi school distinguishes between digging in one's own property, in the courtyard (finā') that is owned or under right, and in shared or public spaces. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the maxim that one is not liable for acts done within one's own right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is digging a well. The default ruling: no liability if done in owned property because there is no transgression (lā ta'addī).
Ownership gives the right to use the land.
2
Examine the courtyard (finā') exception
If the finā' is owned by the digger or he has the right to dig (e.g., by imam's permission), he is not a transgressor and is not liable.
The finā' is considered under the owner's disposal for the benefit of the house.
3
Identify when liability arises
If the finā' belongs to the Muslim community or is a shared non-through street (sikkah ghayr nāfidhah), the digger becomes a transgressor (musabbib muta'addī) and is liable.
Shared spaces create a transgressive act because the digger has no individual right.
4
Confirm the relied-upon position
The text ends with 'wa hādhā saḥīḥ' (this is correct), affirming the position that liability attaches in shared or public finā'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا اپنے ملک یا گھر کے فناء میں کنواں کھودا ضامن نہ ہوگا وكذا إن حفر في ملكه لم يضمن لأنه غير متعد وكذا إذا حفر فى فناء داره لأن له ذالك لمصلحة داره والفناء فى تصرفه وقيل هذا إذا كان الفناء مملوكا له أو كان له حق الجفر فيه لأنه غير متعد أما إذا كان لجماعة المسلمين أو مشتركا بأن كان في سكة غير نافذة فإنه يضمنه لأنه مسبب متعد وهذا صحيح ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر اپنی ملک میں کنواں کھودا تو ضامن نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ وہ متعدی نہیں ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ اس نے اپنے گھر کی فناء میں کھودا اس لئے کہ اس کو کھوڑ نے کا حق اپنے گھر کی مصلحت کے لئے اور فناء اس کے تصرف میں ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ( عدم منمان) جب ہے جب کہ فناء اس کی مملوک ہو یا اس کو اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق ہو اس لئے کہ وہ غیر متعدی ہے بہر حال جب وہ جماعت مسلمین کے لئے ہو یا مشترک ہو اس طریقہ پر کہ وہ سکہ غیر نافذہ میں ہو تو وہ اس کا ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ ایسا مسبب ہے جو متعدی ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے۔ تشریح جس طرح امور مذکورہ بالا باذن امام کرنے کی صورت میں ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اپنی ملوکہ زمین میں یہ تصرفات کرے تو بھی ضمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں اس کی جانب سے کوئی متعدی نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر راستہ سے ہٹ کر اپنے گھر کے آنگن میں جس کو فناء دار سے تعبیر کیا گیا ہے مذکورہ تصرفات کئے ہیں تو اس میں دیکھا جائے گا کہ وہ اس کا مملوک ہے یا نہیں مملوک ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر غیر مملوک ہے لیکن باذن امام یا لوگوں کے لئے مضر نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو کنواں وغیرہ کھود نے کا اس میں حق حاصل ہے تب بھی اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے۔
If he digs a well in his own property or the courtyard of his house, he will not be liable. And similarly if he digs in his property, he is not liable because he is not a transgressor. And similarly if he digs in the courtyard of his house, because he has that right for the benefit of his house, and the courtyard is under his disposition. It is said: this (non-liability) is when the courtyard is owned by him or he has the right to dig therein, because he is not a transgressor. But if it is for the Muslim community or shared, as in a non-through street, then he is liable for it because he is a causative agent who is a transgressor, and this is correct. Translation: And similarly if he dug a well in his own property, he will not be liable because he is not a transgressor. And similarly when he dug in his house's courtyard, because he has the right to dig for his house's benefit and the courtyard is under his disposition. It is said: this non-liability is when the courtyard is owned by him or he has the right to dig therein, because he is not a transgressor. In any case, when it is for the Muslim community or shared in a non-through street, then he is liable for it because he is a causative agent who is a transgressor, and this is correct. Explanation: Just as in the above matters with the imam's permission there is no liability, similarly if he does these acts in his owned land, there is no liability because there is no transgression from his side. And if he does these acts in his house's courtyard (fina' ad-dar), it is considered whether it is owned by him or not. If owned, no liability. If not owned but he has the right to dig by the imam's permission or because it is not harmful to people, then also no liability, because there is no transgression.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation on liability for digging a well in one's own property (milk) or courtyard (finā'). It states that if one digs in his owned land, there is no liability because there is no transgression (lā ta'addī). Similarly, digging in the finā' (courtyard) of his house is without liability if the finā' is owned by him or he has a right to dig there, as it serves the benefit of his house. However, if the finā' is for the Muslim community (jamā'at al-muslimīn) or is shared (mushtarak) such as in a non-through street (sikkah ghayr nāfidhah), then the digger is liable because he becomes a causative agent (musabbib) who is a transgressor (muta'addī). The note 'wa hādhā saḥīḥ' indicates that this is the correct and relied-upon position. The commentary then elaborates that the principle is the same as the previous lesson: permission or ownership removes transgression.

Key Terms
فناء (finā'): The courtyard or open space attached to a house, used for the benefit of the house.
سكة غير نافذة (sikkah ghayr nāfidhah): A dead-end street or alley that is not a throughway, often shared by residents.
مسبب (musabbib): A causative agent; one who sets up a cause that indirectly leads to harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid digs a well in the finā' (courtyard) of his house, which is owned by him. Someone falls in and dies. Is Zaid liable?
A) Yes, because death occurred.
B) No, because the finā' is his property and he has the right to dig.
C) Yes, because he should have covered it.
D) No, because the victim was trespassing.

Key Takeaway
Liability for digging a well turns on ownership or right: no transgression means no liability; in shared spaces, transgression arises and liability is wajib.

Liability for Death by Hunger or Grief After Falling into a Well
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability when a person dies of hunger or grief after falling into a well in a public road

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on liability for death by hunger or grief after falling into a well, and explain the legal reasoning (ʿillah) behind each imam's view.

Core Idea
Liability depends on direct causation: Abu Hanifa requires death from the fall itself, while others differ on indirect causes.

In Hanafi tort law, the digger of an unlawfully placed well is liable only if the death results directly from the fall. But what if the victim dies from hunger or grief after the fall? The three founding imams of the madhhab—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—disagree on whether such indirect causes trigger liability. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A well is dug unlawfully in a public road. A person falls in and dies. The cause of death is either hunger or grief, not the physical impact of the fall.
This scenario tests the principle of causation (sababiyyah).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa holds no liability in either case. The death is due to an internal cause (maʿnā fī nafsihi) within the victim, not directly from the fall. Liability only arises if death is min al-wuqūʿ (from the fall itself).
The key phrase: 'māta li-maʿnā fī nafsihi'.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on hunger (no liability) because hunger is not specific to the well. However, for grief, he holds the digger liable because grief has no cause other than the fall (lā sabab lil-ghamm siwā al-wuqūʿ).
Abu Yusuf differentiates between two types of indirect causes.
4
State Muhammad's position and its basis
Muhammad holds the digger liable in both cases. He argues that both hunger and grief are caused by the fall: without the fall, the victim would have had access to food and would not have experienced such distress.
Muhammad sees a chain of causation: fall → confinement → hunger/grief.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a case of death by grief, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad would impose liability, while Abu Hanifa would not. In a case of death by hunger, only Muhammad imposes liability.
This affects who pays diyah (blood money).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو حفر في الطريق ومات الواقع فيه جوعا أو غما لاضمان على الحافر عند أبي حنيفة لأنه مات لمعنى في نفسه والضمان إنما يجب إذا مات من الوقوع وقال أبويوسف إن مات جوعا فكذالك وإن مات غما فالحافر ضامن له لأنه لاسبب للغم سوى الوقوع أما الجوع فلايختص بالبير وقال محمد هو ضامن في الوجوه كلها لأنه إنما حدث بسبب الوقوع إذ لولاه لكان الطعام قريبا منه ترجمہ اور اگر راستہ میں کنواں کھودا اور اس میں گرنے والا بھوک یا غم کی وجہ سے مرگیا تو حافر پر ضمان نہ ہوگا ہم بوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ وہ ایسے سبب سے مرا ہے جو کرنے والے کے نفس میں ہے اور ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے جب کہ وہ گرنے کی وجہ سے مرے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اگر بھوک کی وجہ سے مرے تو ایسے ہی ہے ( یعنی ضمان نہیں ہے) اور اگر غم کی وجہ سے مرے تو حافر کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ وہ تمام صورتوں میں ضامن ہے اس لئے کہ بھوک پیدا ہوئی ہے گرنے کے سبب سے اس لئے کہ اگر یہ (کنویں میں گرنا ) نہ ہوتا تو کھانا اس کے قریب ہوتا۔ تشریح زید نے راستہ میں جہاں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں تھا، کنواں کھودا جس میں خالد گر کر مر گیا۔ تو اگر موت کا سبب گرنا ہو تو منمان واجب ہوگا لیکن اگر وہ گرنے کی وجہ سے نہ مرا ہو بلکہ دہشت کی وجہ سے یا بھوک کی وجہ سے مرا ہو تو اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بھوک اور غم کی وجہ سے مرنے کی صورت میں حاضر پر ضمان نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے خالد خودمرا ہو اور کنواں کھودنے والے پر اسی صورت میں ضمان ہوگا جب کہ صرف گرنے کی وجہ سے مرجائے تا کہ حافر کنویں میں دھکا دینے والا شمار کیا
And if he dug a well in the road and the one who fell into it died of hunger or grief, there is no liability upon the digger according to Abu Hanifa, because he died due to a meaning within himself, and liability is only obligatory if he dies from the fall. Abu Yusuf said: if he died of hunger, the same [no liability]; if he died of grief, the digger is liable because the cause of grief is nothing other than the fall; as for hunger, it is not specific to the well. Muhammad said: he is liable in all cases because it occurred due to the fall, for if it were not for the fall, food would have been near him. Translation: And if he dug a well in the road and the one who fell into it died of hunger or grief, there is no liability upon the digger according to Abu Hanifa, because he died due to a cause within himself (i.e., his own condition), and liability is only obligatory if he dies from the fall. Abu Yusuf said: if he died of hunger, similarly no liability; if he died of grief, the digger is liable because the cause of grief is nothing other than the fall; as for hunger, it is not specific to the well. Muhammad said: he is liable in all cases because the death occurred due to the fall, for if he had not fallen, food would have been close to him. Explanation: Zaid dug a well in the road where he had no right, and Khalid fell in and died. If the cause of death is the fall, liability is wajib. But if he did not die from the fall but from fright or hunger, there is ikhtilaf. According to Abu Hanifa, no liability for hunger/grief because it is as if Khalid died by himself; liability only if the fall itself caused death.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding liability when a person dies of hunger or grief after falling into a well dug unlawfully in a public road. Three positions are clearly given: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa holds that there is no liability (lā ḍamān) in both cases because the death resulted from an internal cause (ma'nā fī nafsihi) within the victim, not directly from the fall; liability only arises if death is from the fall itself. (2) Imam Abu Yusuf differentiates: if death is from hunger, no liability; if from grief, the digger is liable because grief has no other cause than the fall (the shock and distress are directly linked to the fall), whereas hunger could have been alleviated if food were available. (3) Imam Muhammad holds the digger liable in all cases because the hunger or grief was caused by the fall; without the fall, the victim would have had access to food. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the explanation indicates that the default ruling is liability only for direct death from falling. This dispute highlights the Hanafi methodology of causal connection (sababiyyah) in tort law.

Key Terms
الجوع (al-jū'): Hunger; death due to starvation after falling into a well.
الغم (al-ghamm): Grief or distress; death due to emotional shock from falling.
الوقوع (al-wuqū'): The act of falling into the well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a person falls into a well dug unlawfully and dies of grief (ghamm), is the digger liable?
A) Yes, because grief is directly caused by the fall.
B) No, because grief is an internal condition.
C) Only if the well was dug without permission.
D) No, because the victim's grief is unrelated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tort law, liability for death after a fall requires direct causation; differences among the imams turn on whether internal conditions like hunger or grief are considered direct results of the fall.
