Liability for Digging a Well: The Principle of Non-Transgression
Ruling on liability for digging well in own property or fina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on liability for digging a well in one's own property or fina, and identify the condition of transgression that triggers liability.

Core Idea
No liability without transgression: ownership or right to use absolves the digger.

In Hanafi tort law, causing harm does not automatically create liability. The key is whether the act was transgressive (muta'addi). This lesson examines the classical ruling on digging a well in one's own property or courtyard (fina). Understanding this principle clarifies many everyday scenarios where harm results from permissible actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses digging a well in one's own property (milk) or courtyard (fina). The default ruling is that the digger is not liable for any subsequent harm because he is not transgressing.
The act itself is permissible (mubah).
2
Determine the condition of ownership or right
For the fina, note that non-liability applies only if the fina is owned by the digger or if he has a recognized right to dig (e.g., permission from the imam or no harm to others).
The right must be established; mere use is not enough.
3
Identify the exception that triggers liability
If the well is dug in shared community land or a public alley, the digger becomes liable because his action is transgressive (muta'addi).
The passage explicitly states: 'when it is for the Muslim community or shared... then he will be liable.'
4
Understand the role of transgression (ta'addi)
The deciding factor is whether the digger exceeded his rights. Ownership or a proper right makes the act non-transgressive; lack of such right or harm to public interest makes it transgressive and liable.
Ta'addi is the core concept: an action that oversteps legal boundaries.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may hold the digger liable even in his own property if the well is near a public path or causes foreseeable harm, emphasizing the principle of harming others over ownership rights.
This difference changes the outcome in marginal cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر اپنی ملک میں کنواں کھودا تو ضامن نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ وہ متعدی نہیں ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ اس نے اپنے گھر کی فناء میں کھودا اس لئے کہ اس کو کھودنے کا حق اپنے گھر کی مصلحت کے لئے اور فناء اس کے تصرف میں ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ (عدم ضمان) جب ہے جب کہ فناء اس کی مملوک ہو یا اس کو اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق ہو اس لئے کہ وہ غیر متعدی ہے بہر حال جب وہ جماعت مسلمین کے لئے ہو یا مشترک ہو اس طریقہ پر کہ وہ سکہ غیر نافذہ میں ہو تو وہ اس کا ضامن ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ ایسا مسبب ہے جو متعدی ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے۔
تشریح جس طرح امور مذکورہ بالا باذن امام کرنے کی صورت میں ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اپنی ملوکہ زمین میں یہ تصرفات کرے تو بھی ضمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں اس کی جانب سے کوئی متعدی نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر راستہ سے ہٹ کر اپنے گھر کے آنگن میں جس کو فناء دار سے تعبیر کیا گیا ہے مذکورہ تصرفات کئے ہیں تو اس میں دیکھا جائے گا کہ وہ اس کا مملوک ہے یا نہیں مملوک ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر غیر مملوک ہے لیکن باذن امام یا لوگوں کے لئے مضر نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو کنواں وغیرہ کھودنے کا اس میں حق حاصل ہے تب بھی اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے۔
Translation: And similarly, if he dug a well in his own property, he will not be liable because he is not transgressing. And similarly, when he dug in the courtyard of his house, because he has the right to dig for the benefit of his house and the courtyard is under his disposal. And it has been said that this (non-liability) is when the courtyard is owned by him or he has the right to dig a well in it, because he is not transgressing. In any case, when it is for the Muslim community or shared in a way that it is in a non-viable alley, then he will be liable because it is a cause that is transgressive. And this is correct.
Elaboration: Just as in the aforementioned matters, if done with the permission of the imam, liability is not obligatory; similarly, if he performs these dispositions in his own owned land, liability will not be incurred because there is no transgression from his side. And if, away from the path, in the courtyard of his house, which is called the fina of the house, he performed the aforementioned dispositions, then it will be considered whether it is owned by him or not. If it is owned, there will be no liability upon him. And if it is not owned, but he has the right to dig a well etc. in it by the permission of the imam or because it is not harmful to people, then too liability will not be obligatory upon him because now there is no transgression from his side.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with elaboration. The author first states the general rule: if one digs a well in his own property, he is not liable for any harm because he has ownership rights and is not transgressing. The same applies if he digs in the courtyard (fina) of his house, provided the courtyard is either owned by him or he has a right to dig there (e.g., by permission of the imam or because it does not harm others). However, if the well is dug in a place belonging to the Muslim community or a shared property in a dead-end alley, he becomes liable because his action is transgressive. The commentary reinforces this, emphasizing that the key is transgression (ta'addi): if the digger has a right to the land and the act does not harm others, no liability; otherwise, liability attaches.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The courtyard or open space attached to a house, which is under the owner's disposal but may not necessarily be owned.
متعدی (muta'addī): Transgressive; an action that exceeds one's rights and causes harm to others.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation or blood money due to harm caused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when does a person who digs a well in his own courtyard become liable for resulting harm?
A) Always, because harm was caused.
B) When the courtyard is not owned by him and he has no right to dig.
C) Only if he was paid to dig it.
D) When the well is deeper than 10 meters.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability for harm from digging a well hinges on transgression (ta'addi), not mere causation; ownership or a recognized right negates transgression.

Liability for Death by Hunger or Grief from a Well in a Public Path
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for indirect death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability for death caused indirectly by hunger or grief after falling into a well dug in a public path, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Liability for indirect death requires direct causation; each imam defines the causal chain differently.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a digger of a well in a public path is liable when the victim dies not from the fall itself but from hunger or grief while trapped. The three Hanafi imams differ on how to trace the cause of death, illustrating the school's method of distinguishing direct from indirect causation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply causation principles in tort liability cases within the Hanafi fiqh framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
What is the act that triggers potential liability? The act is digging a well in a public path (where one has no right). The victim falls in but does not die from the fall; instead, death occurs from hunger or grief while trapped. Determine the baseline ruling: if death is directly from the fall, all agree liability exists.
2
State the common ground among the imams
All three imams agree that if death is directly caused by the fall (e.g., impact), the digger is liable. The dispute is only about indirect causes (hunger and grief). Recognize that the disagreement is over the scope of causation.
3
Outline each imam's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa: no liability because death from hunger/grief is from an internal meaning (ma'na fi nafsihi), not from the fall. Abu Yusuf: no liability for hunger (since hunger could occur anywhere), but liability for grief (since grief is uniquely caused by the fall). Muhammad: liability for both because both hunger and grief are consequences of the fall; without the fall, food would have been available and grief would not have occurred.
Note the key distinction: Abu Yusuf differentiates between hunger and grief based on specificity to the well.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The text leads with Abu Hanifa's view, indicating it is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the madhhab. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): In a case of death from hunger, only Muhammad imposes liability; in death from grief, Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes. The operative fatwa follows Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر راستہ میں کنواں کھودا اور اس میں گرنے والا بھوک یا غم کی وجہ سے مرگیا تو حافر پر ضمان نہ ہوگا ہم بوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ وہ ایسے سبب سے مرا ہے جو کرنے والے کے نفس میں ہے اور ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے جب کہ وہ گرنے کی وجہ سے مرے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اگر بھوک کی وجہ سے مرے تو ایسے ہی ہے ( یعنی ضمان نہیں ہے) اور اگر غم کی وجہ سے مرے تو حافر کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ وہ تمام صورتوں میں ضامن ہے اس لئے کہ بھوک پیدا ہوئی ہے گرنے کے سبب سے اس لئے کہ اگر یہ (کنویں میں گرنا ) نہ ہوتا تو کھانا اس کے قریب ہوتا۔
تشریح زید نے راستہ میں جہاں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں تھا، کنواں کھودا جس میں خالد گر کر مر گیا۔ تو اگر موت کا سبب گرنا ہو تو ضمان واجب ہوگا لیکن اگر وہ گرنے کی وجہ سے نہ مرا ہو بلکہ دہشت کی وجہ سے یا بھوک کی وجہ سے مرا ہو تو اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بھوک اور غم کی وجہ سے مرنے کی صورت میں حاضر پر ضمان نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے خالد خودمرا ہو اور کنواں کھودنے والے پر اسی صورت میں ضمان ہوگا جب کہ صرف گرنے کی وجہ سے مرجائے تا کہ حافر کنویں میں دھکا دینے والا شمار کیا جاسکے۔
اور امام ابو یوسف کا فرمان یہ ہے کہ بھوک اور غم میں فرق ہے کیونکہ بھوک میں زید کا کوئی دخل نہیں لیکن غم اور دہشت میں زید کا دخل ہے کیونکہ خالد کو جو خوف و ہراس و دہشت طاری ہوتی ہے اس کا سبب فقط کنویں میں گرنا ہے۔ اس لئے بھوک کی صورت میں تو زید پر ضمان نہ ہوگا البتہ غم کی صورت میں ضمان ہوگا۔
اور امام محمدکا فرمان یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ جس طرح غم کا سبب کنویں میں گرنا ہے اسی طرح بھوک کا سبب بھی کنویں میں گرنا ہے کیونکہ اگر وہ کنویں میں نہ ہوتا تو کوئی بھی اس کو کھانا کھلا دیتا۔
And if he dug a well in the road, and the one who fell into it died of hunger or grief, there is no liability on the digger according to Abu Hanifa, because he died from a meaning within himself, and liability is only obligatory if he died from the fall. Abu Yusuf said: if he died of hunger, then similarly (no liability); if he died of grief, then the digger is liable for him because there is no cause of grief other than the fall. As for hunger, it is not specific to the well. Muhammad said: he is liable in all aspects because it (the death) happened due to the fall; for if not for it, food would have been near him.
Translation and elaboration.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a person who digs a well in a public road (where he has no right) when the victim dies not directly from the fall but from hunger or grief suffered while trapped. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: liability only if death is directly caused by the fall itself. If death occurs from hunger or grief (conditions arising from the victim's own state), the digger is not liable because the cause of death is internal. Abu Yusuf differentiates between hunger and grief: hunger is not specific to the well (the victim could have died of hunger elsewhere), so no liability; but grief is directly caused by the fall, so the digger is liable for grief-induced death. Muhammad holds the digger liable in both cases, arguing that both hunger and grief are consequences of the fall; had the victim not fallen, he would have had access to food and would not have grieved. The commentary of Ashraf al-Hidaya explains this with an example of Zaid digging a well where Khalid falls and dies. It clarifies that if death is from the fall itself, all agree on liability. The disagreement is only when death is from hunger or fright (grief). The elaboration presents each imam's reasoning.

Key Terms
بئر (bi'r): A well; in this context, a pit dug in the ground.
حافر (ḥāfir): The one who digs the well; the digger.
واقع (wāqi'): The one who falls into the well; the victim.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the indirect cause that leads to the death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Digger is liable.
B) Digger is not liable.
C) Digger is liable only if the victim dies of grief.
D) Digger is liable according to Imam Muhammad but not according to the mufta bihi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that indirect death from hunger or grief after falling into a well dug in a public path does not make the digger liable; only direct death from the fall does.

Liability of Employer vs Deceived Workers in Digging
Ruling on liability with analogy to slaughter case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on liability for hired workers when they are deceived by the employer's transgression, and distinguish it from the case of ordered slaughter.

Core Idea
Liability shifts to the employer when hired workers are deceived and the employer is the transgressor.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Al-Hidayah that addresses a nuanced liability scenario: an employer hires workers to dig a well in what he claims is his courtyard (fina), but the fina actually belongs to someone else. The workers, unaware, dig the well, and someone falls in and dies. Who bears the blood money? The Hanafi school places liability squarely on the employer, not the workers, due to the employer's transgression and the workers' deception. The ruling is derived by way of qiyas (analogy) to a case of ordered slaughter, but with a critical distinction that changes the outcome. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to apply causation principles (mubashir vs. musabbib) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage to understand the factual scenario: hired workers dig a well in a non-owned fina without knowledge. The ruling states the employer is liable, not the workers. Note the phrase 'if they did not know' — this is the key condition.
The workers' ignorance is essential; if they knew, the ruling might differ.
2
Understand the legal reason (sabab) for the ruling
The text explains that the workers were deceived (maghrūrūn). Their contract was valid in appearance, so their action is attributed to the employer. The employer is the transgressor (muta'addi), while the workers are not.
Deception (ghurūr) transfers liability from the direct agent to the deceiver.
3
Compare with the analogous case of ordered slaughter
The author compares to a case where one orders another to slaughter a sheep that turns out to belong to another. In that case, the slaughterer (direct agent) is initially liable and then recovers from the orderer. Note the difference: there, the slaughterer is a direct agent (mubashir); here, both employer and worker are causes (musabbib).
The distinction hinges on mubasharah vs. tasabbub.
4
Identify the distinction that changes the result
In the slaughter case, the direct agent is the mubashir, so he is liable first. In the digging case, the workers are not direct agents of the harm (the well is the cause), and they are not transgressing. The employer is the only transgressor. Therefore, liability falls on him from the start.
The concept of ta'addī (transgression) becomes the decisive factor.
5
Apply the ruling to similar scenarios
Consider variations: what if the workers knew the fina was not the employer's? What if the employer believed it was his own? The ruling would likely change. Practice analyzing these using the same principles.
The ruling is specific to the condition of the workers' ignorance and the employer's transgression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن استأجر أجراء فحفروها له في غير فنائه فذالك على المستأجر ولا شيء على الاجراء إن لم يعلموا أنها فى غير فنائه لأن الإجارة صحت ظاهرة إذا لم يعلموا فنقل فعلهم إليه لأنهم كانوا مغرورين فصار كما إذا أمر آخر بذبح هذه الشاة فذبحها ثم ظهر أن الشاة لغيره إلا أن هناك يضمن المأمور ويرجع على الآمر لأن الذابح مباشر والآمر مسبب والترجيح للمباشرة فيضمن ويرجع للغرور وهنا يجب الضمان على المستأجر ابتداء لأن كل واحد منهما مسبب والأجير غير متعد والمستأجر متعد فترجح جانبه
ترجمہ حضرت مصنف صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا اور اگر اس نے کچھ اجیر رکھے پس انہوں نے اس کے لئے ایک کنواں کھود دیا اس کی غیر فناء میں پس ضمان مستاجر پر ہوگا او مزدوروں پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اگر انہیں یہ بات معلوم نہ ہو کہ یہ کنواں کھودنا) اس کی فناء کے غیر میں ہے اس لئے کہ اجارہ اس کے ظاہر کے اعتبار سے صحیح ہو گیا جب کہ انہیں علم نہ ہو تو ان کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ مستاجر کی جانب سے ) دھوکہ دیتے ہوئے ہیں پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی دوسر نے کسی شخص کو حکم دیا اس بکری کو ذبح کرنے کا پس اس نے اس کو ذبح کر دیا پھر یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ بکری اس کے غیر کی ہے مگر یہاں ( ذبیح کے مسئلہ میں ) مامور ( ذابح ) ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح آمر کی جانب رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ ذابح مباشر ہے اور آمر مسبب ہے اور ترجیح مباشرت کو ہوتی ہے تو ذابح ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح دھوکہ کی وجہ سے آمر پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہاں ضمان پہلے ہی سے مستاجر پر واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مسبب ہے اور اجیر غیر متعدی ہے اور مستاجر متعدی ہے پس مستاجر کی جانب راجح ہو گئی۔
تشریح زید نے کچھ مزدوروں کو اجیر رکھا تا کہ فناء میں کنواں کھودیں انہوں نے کنواں کھودا اور اس کے اندر کوئی گر کر مر گیا، پہلے سے یہ بات مشہور نہ تھی کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے اب معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان کس پر واجب ہوگا ؟
تو فرمایا کہ صورت مذکورہ میں زید پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مزدوروں پر نہ ہو گا کیونکہ جب مزدوروں کو یہ علم نہیں ہے کہ یہ فنا کسی اور کی ہے بلکہ وہ اس کو زید کی فناء سمجھے ہوئے ہیں تو اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا اور جب اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا تو مزدوروں کا فعل مستاجر کی طرح منتقل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں زید ( مستاجر ) نے ان کو دھوکہ دیا ہے۔ اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کو حکم دیا کہ اس بکری کو ذبح کر دے اس نے ذبح کر دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بکری ساجد کی ہے تو
He said: And if he hired workers and they dug a well for him in other than his courtyard, then the liability is on the employer, and nothing on the workers if they did not know that it was in other than his courtyard, because the hire contract was valid apparently when they did not know; so their action is transferred to him because they were deceived. So it becomes like the case where one ordered another to slaughter this sheep, and he slaughtered it, then it appeared that the sheep belonged to someone else. Except that there the commanded (slaughterer) is liable and he recovers from the orderer, because the slaughterer is the direct agent (mubashir) and the orderer is the cause (musabbib), and precedence is given to direct agency, so the slaughterer is liable and he recovers due to deception. Here liability is initially obligatory on the employer because each of them is a cause, and the hired worker is not transgressing while the employer is transgressing, so his side is preponderant.
Elaboration: Zaid hired some workers to dig a well in the courtyard (fina). They dug the well and someone fell in and died. It was not previously known that the fina was not Zaid's; now it became known that it is not Zaid's fina. So on whom is liability? He said: In the described case, liability will be on Zaid, not on the workers, because when the workers did not know that this fina belonged to someone else but thought it was Zaid's, the hire was valid, and when the hire is valid, the workers' action is transferred to the employer. Because Zaid (the employer) deceived them. An example: Zaid ordered Khalid to slaughter this sheep; he slaughtered it; then it appeared that the sheep belonged to Sajid.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof by analogy. The author of Hidayah states: If an employer hires workers to dig a well in his courtyard (fina) but the courtyard actually belongs to someone else, and the workers are unaware, then the employer is liable for any harm (e.g., someone falling in) because the workers are deceived. The workers' actions are attributed to the employer because they acted under a valid contract that appeared legitimate. The ruling is contrasted with the case of ordered slaughter: there, the direct slaughterer is initially liable and then recovers from the orderer due to deception, because the slaughterer is the direct agent (mubashir) and the orderer is the cause (musabbib). Here, both (employer and worker) are causes, but the worker is not transgressing (ghayr muta'addi) while the employer is transgressing (muta'addi), so liability falls directly on the employer. The commentary gives a concrete example: Zaid hires workers to dig in what he claims is his fina; after someone dies, it turns out the fina was not Zaid's. The workers are not liable because they were deceived; Zaid is liable as the transgressor.

Key Terms
مستأجر (musta'jir): The employer who hires workers for a specific task.
أجير (ajīr): A hired worker; in this context, a laborer hired to dig.
مباشر (mubāshir): The direct agent who physically performs the act causing harm.
مسبب (musabbib): The indirect cause who sets in motion the chain of events leading to harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the hired workers not liable in the case of digging a well in a non-owned fina?
A) Because they were paid for the work.
B) Because they were unaware that the fina was not the employer's, and the employer transgressed.
C) Because they did not actually dig the well.
D) Because the employer ordered them to dig.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when hired workers are deceived and the employer is the transgressor, liability falls on the employer, not the workers, due to the principle that transgression outweighs direct agency when neither is a direct cause.

Diyat — Blood Money

Liability for Death by Hunger vs. Grief After a Fall
Intra-Hanafi dispute on causation in diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on liability for hunger vs. grief after a fall, and identify the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
The same fall can cause different outcomes—liability depends on how directly the action connects to the death.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding liability for death caused by falling into a well. The dispute hinges on whether the mode of death—hunger or grief—affects causation. We will analyse the reasoning of each imam and understand the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Set the scenario
A person digs a well, another falls in and dies. The cause of death is either hunger (starvation) or grief/fear. Identify the parties: the digger (Zaid) and the victim (Khalid).
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf says: in hunger, Zaid has no involvement—the victim simply starved, not directly caused by the fall. In grief/fear, the emotional distress is directly caused by the fall, so Zaid is liable.
Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on direct causation.
3
State Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad says: both hunger and grief are caused by the fall because without the fall neither would occur. The fall is the common cause, so Zaid is liable in both cases.
Muhammad uses a 'but-for' causation analysis.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if the victim died of hunger, Abu Yusuf says no diyat, Muhammad says diyat is wajib. The mufta bihi is not specified in this text.
The dispute affects whether the digger must pay blood money.
5
Reflect on causation theory
The dispute highlights that causation in Hanafi law is not purely physical; it involves legal attribution (isnad). The two imams differ on what constitutes a sufficient causal link.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور امام ابو یوسف کا فرمان یہ ہے کہ بھوک اور غم میں فرق ہے کیونکہ بھوک میں زید کا کوئی دخل نہیں لیکن غم اور دہشت میں زید کا دخل ہے کیونکہ خالد کو جو خوف و ہراس و دہشت طاری ہوتی ہے اس کا سبب فقط کنویں میں گرنا ہے۔ اس لئے بھوک کی صورت میں تو زید پر ضمان نہ ہوگا البتہ غم کی صورت میں ضمان ہوگا۔ اور امام محمدکا فرمان یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں ضمان واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ جس طرح غم کا سبب کنویں میں گرنا ہے اسی طرح بھوک کا سبب بھی کنویں میں گرنا ہے کیونکہ اگر وہ کنویں میں نہ ہوتا تو کوئی بھی اس کو کھانا کھلا دیتا۔
And Imam Abu Yusuf's command is that there is a difference between hunger and grief because in hunger Zaid has no involvement, but in grief and terror Zaid has involvement because the fear, horror, and terror that overcome Khalid are caused only by falling into the well. Therefore, in the case of hunger, Zaid will not be liable, but in the case of grief, he will be liable. And Imam Muhammad's command is that in both cases liability is obligatory because just as grief is caused by falling into the well, similarly hunger is also caused by falling into the well because if he were not in the well, someone would have fed him.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the liability of a person (Zaid) who digs a well, causing another (Khalid) to fall into it, leading to death. The issue is whether liability (diyat) is affected by the manner of death: if the victim died of hunger (being trapped) or of grief/fear. Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes: in hunger, Zaid has no direct role—the victim simply starved, which is not caused by the fall alone; but in grief/fear, the emotional distress is directly caused by the fall, so Zaid is liable. Imam Muhammad argues both are caused by the fall: without the fall, neither hunger nor grief would have occurred, because if the victim were not trapped, he would have been fed. Thus, the fall is the effective cause for both outcomes, so liability attaches in both cases. The text does not mention Imam Abu Hanifa's view or a tarjih between the two Sahibayn.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability for blood money (diyat) when death is caused by one's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, in which scenario does the well-digger bear liability?
A) When the victim dies of hunger
B) When the victim dies of grief or fear
C) In both scenarios
D) In neither scenario

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad shows that causation in diyat is not mechanical; the mode of death can affect whether the act is considered the legal cause.

Liability Where Workers Are Unaware of Non-Ownership
First scenario: liability when workers unaware

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when hired workers dig on non-owned property without knowledge, and explain the legal distinction from the sheep-slaughter analogy.

Core Idea
When workers are deceived, liability shifts to the hirer as the transgressing indirect cause.

This lesson examines the first scenario from al-Hidayah: hired workers dig a well on land that is not their employer's, but they do not know this. The ruling is that the employer (hirer) bears full liability, not the workers. We will unpack the reasoning, which involves a careful comparison with the analogous case of a commanded slaughter of a misidentified sheep, and understand why the outcome differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the first ruling: when hired workers dig a well in a place that is not the hirer's courtyard (fana'), and they are unaware, the liability (daman) is on the hirer. Note the condition: workers did not know.
Key condition: ignorance of the workers.
2
Analyze the legal reasoning
The text gives two reasons: the hire contract appeared valid to the workers, so their action is transferred to the hirer; and the workers were deceived (maghrurin). Understand the concept of 'transfer of action' (naql al-fi'l) when a contract is apparently valid.
The deception creates a legal nexus.
3
Compare with the sheep-slaughter analogy
The author compares to a case where a person orders another to slaughter a sheep that turns out to belong to a third party. In that case, the slaughterer (direct agent) is liable first, then recovers from the orderer. Identify the difference: in the well case, both hirer and worker are indirect causes (musabbib), not direct agent vs. indirect cause.
Crucial distinction: mubashir vs. musabbib.
4
Apply the principle of transgression (ta'addi)
In the well case, the hirer is a transgressor (muta'addi) because he commanded an act on land he does not own; the workers are not transgressors. Therefore, the hirer's side is preponderant, and liability attaches to him directly.
Ta'addi overrides the usual preference for direct agency.
5
Derive the general ruling
Conclude: when a hirer engages workers for an act on non-owned property without their knowledge, the hirer is liable for any harm caused, because he is the transgressing indirect cause.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستاجر مزدوروں سے غیر فناء میں کنواں کھدوایا پھر کوئی مر گیا توضمان کس پر ہے

قال وإن استأجر أجراء فحفروها له في غير فنائه فذالك على المستأجر ولا شيء على الاجراء إن لم يعلموا أنها فى غير فنائه لأن الإجارة صحت ظاهرة إذا لم يعلموا فنقل فعلهم إليه لأنهم كانوا مغرورين فصار كما إذا أمر آخر بذبح هذه الشاة فذبحها ثم ظهر أن الشاة لغيره إلا أن هناك يضمن المأمور ويرجع على الآمر لأن الذابح مباشر والآمر مسبب والترجيح للمباشرة فيضمن ويرجع للغرور وهنا يجب الضمان على المستأجر ابتداء لأن كل واحد منهما مسبب والأجير غير متعد والمستأجر متعد فترجح جانبه

ترجمہ حضرت مصنف صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا اور اگر اس نے کچھ اجیر رکھے پس انہوں نے اس کے لئے ایک کنواں کھود دیا اس کی غیر فناء میں پس ضمان مستاجر پر ہوگا او مزدوروں پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اگر انہیں یہ بات معلوم نہ ہو کہ یہ کنواں کھودنا ) اس کی فناء کے غیر میں ہے اس لئے کہ اجارہ اس کے ظاہر کے اعتبار سے صحیح ہو گیا جب کہ انہیں علم نہ ہو تو ان کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ مستاجر کی جانب سے ) دھوکہ دیتے ہوئے ہیں پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی دوسر نے کسی شخص کو حکم کیا اس بکری کو ذبح کرنے کا پس اس نے اس کو ذبح کر دیا پھر یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ بکری اس کے غیر کی ہے مگر یہاں ( ذبیح کے مسئلہ میں ) مامور ( ذالخ ) ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح آمر کی جانب رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ ذابح مباشر ہے اور آمر مسبب ہے اور ترجیح مباشرت کو ہوتی ہے تو ذابح ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح دھو کہ کی وجہ سے آمر پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہاں ضمان پہلے ہی سے مستاجر پر واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مسبب ہے اور اجیر غیر متعدی ہے اور مستاجر متعدی ہے پس مستاجر کی جانب راجح ہو گئی۔

تشریح زید نے کچھ مزدوروں کو اجیر رکھا تا کہ فناء میں کنواں کھودیں انہوں نے کنواں کھودا اور اس کے اندر کوئی گر کر مر گیا، پہلے سے یہ بات مشہور نہ تھی کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے اب معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان کس پر واجب ہوگا ؟

تو فرمایا کہ صورت مذکورہ میں زید پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مزدوروں پر نہ ہو گا کیونکہ جب مزدوروں کو یہ علم نہیں ہے کہ یہ فنا کسی اور کی ہے بلکہ وہ اس کو زید کی فناء سمجھے ہوئے ہیں تو اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا اور جب اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا تو مزدوروں کا فعل مستاجر کی طرح منتقل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں زید ( مستاجر ) نے ان کو دھوکہ دیا ہے۔ اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کو حکم دیا کہ اس بکری کو ذبح کر دے اس نے ذبح کر دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بکری ساجد کی ہے تو یہاں ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اولا ضمان خالد پر واجب ہو گا اور پھر اس ضمان کو زید سے وصول کر لے گا۔ سوال یہاں اولا ضمان خالد پر کیوں واجب ہوا؟
جواب خالد چونکہ ڈائج ہے تو اس کا فعل مباشرت ہے اور زید نے حکم دیا ہے تو وہ فقط مسبب ہے اور مباشر ومسبب میں مباشر کوتر جیح ہوا کرتی ہے اس لئے خالد پر ضمان واجب ہوا لیکن چونکہ اس کو زید نے دھوکہ دیا ہے اس لئے خالد زید سے اس ضمان کو وصول کرے گا۔ سوال یہاں حفر بیر کے مسئلہ میں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے تھا کہ اولا ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوتا اور پھر مزدور اس کو مستاجر واپس لیتا؟
لجواب پہلے مسئلہ میں ذائع کو مباشر ہونے کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی تھی اور یہاں متاجر اور اجیر دونوں سب ہیں تو ترجیح کا مدار تعدی اور ظلم پر رہا اور تعدی صرف مستاجر کی طرف سے ہے اجیر کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔
اس لئے یہاں مستاجر کی جانب کو ترجیح دے کر اسی پر ضمان براہ راست واجب کر دیا۔

اگر ملک نہ ہونے کے علم کے باوجود کھودا تو مزدوروں پر ضمان ہے
وإن علموا ذالك فالضمان على الأجراء لأنه لم يصح أمره بما ليس بمملوك له ولا غرور فبقى الفعل مضافا إليهم.
ترجمہ اور اگر ان کو اس کا علم ہوتو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ مستاجر کا حکم اس چیز کے سلسلہ میں جو اس کی مملوک نہیں ہے اور دھو کہ دینا بھی نہیں ہے تو باقی بچا فعل مضاف انہیں کی طرف۔ تشریح اگر مزدوروں کو معلوم تھا کہ یہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں زید کا حکم صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ زید مالک نہیں ہے اور نہ یہاں زید نے دھوکہ دیا تو اس صورت میں یہ فعل مستاجر کی طرف مضاف نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اجراء کے اوپر ہی ضمان واجب ہوگا۔

مستاجر نے مزدوروں سے کہا کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں انہوں نے کھودا اور ایک آدمی اس میں مر گیا تو ضمان کس پر ہوگا
وإن قال لهم هذا فناى وليس لى فيه حق الحفر فحفروا فمات فيه إنسان فالضمان على الأجراء قياسا لأنهم علموا بفساد الأمر فما غرهم. وفى الاستحسان الضمان على المستأجر لأن كونه فناء له بمنزلة كونه مملوكا له لانطلاق يده فى التصرف فيه من إلقاء الطين والحطب وربط الدابة والركوب وبناء الدكان فكان الأمر بالحفر في ملكه ظاهرا بالنظر إلى ما ذكرنا فكفى ذالك لنقل الفعل إليه.
ترجمہ اور اگر مستاجر نے اجراء سے کہد یا ہو کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں ہے پس انہوں نے کھودا پس اس میں کوئی آدمی مر گیا تو قیا سا ضمان اجزاء پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان کو حکم کے فساد کا علم ہے تو مستاجر نے ان کو دھو کہ نہیں دیا
If he hired workers and they dug a well for him in his non-courtyard (property that is not his), then the liability is on the hirer (musta'jir) and nothing on the workers if they did not know that it was not in his courtyard, because the hire contract became valid on the face of it when they did not know, so their action is transferred to him because they were deceived. This is like if someone ordered another to slaughter this sheep and he slaughtered it, then it appeared that the sheep belonged to someone else—except that there the one ordered is liable and recovers from the orderer, because the slaughterer is the direct agent (mubashir) and the orderer is the indirect cause (musabbib), and preference is given to the direct agent, so he is liable and then recovers due to deception. Here, liability is imposed on the hirer from the beginning because each of them is an indirect cause, but the worker is not a transgressor (ghayr muta'addi) while the hirer is a transgressor (muta'addi), so his side is preponderant. 

If they knew that, then liability is on the workers because his command is not valid regarding something he does not own, and there is no deception, so the action remains attributed to them.

And if he said to them, 'This is my courtyard, but I have no right to dig in it,' and they dug, and a person died in it, then by analogy (qiyas) liability is on the workers because they knew the invalidity of the command, so he did not deceive them. But by juristic preference (istihsan), liability is on the hirer because his ownership of the courtyard is akin to ownership, due to his freedom of disposal—throwing dirt, firewood, tying an animal, riding, building a shop—so the command to dig in his property is apparent in view of what we mentioned, and that suffices to transfer the action to him.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the author (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) regarding liability when hired workers dig a well on land that turns out not to belong to the hirer. It covers three scenarios:
1) Workers unaware: The hirer is liable because the contract appeared valid and the workers were deceived. The action is attributed to the hirer as the indirect cause (musabbib) who is also a transgressor (muta'addi), while the workers are not transgressors. This is distinguished from the sheep slaughter analogy where the direct agent is liable first and then recovers from the orderer due to deception; here both are indirect causes, but the hirer's transgression tips the balance.
2) Workers aware: The hirer's command is invalid (he has no ownership), and there is no deception, so the workers are liable; their action is attributed to them.
3) Hirer says he has no right but workers dig: By qiyas, workers are liable because they knew the command was invalid. By istihsan, the hirer is liable because his de facto control over the courtyard (throwing dirt, etc.) makes it like his property, and the workers were not fully aware of the defect. The istihsan position is likely the relied-upon view, as it considers the practical authority of the hirer.

Key Terms
مباشر (mubashir): Direct agent; the person who physically commits the act causing harm.
مسبب (musabbib): Indirect cause; one who sets in motion a chain of events leading to harm without directly committing the act.
متعد (muta'addi): Transgressor; one who exceeds legal bounds or acts wrongfully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where hired workers dig a well on non-owned property without knowledge, who bears the liability for a resulting death?
A) The workers, because they performed the digging
B) The hirer, because the workers were deceived and the hirer is a transgressor
C) Both are equally liable
D) No one is liable because the workers did not know

Key Takeaway
When hired workers are unaware that the land is not their employer's, the employer is directly liable for harm caused, due to his transgression and the workers' deception.

Liability When Workers Know the Land Is Not the Hirer's
Second scenario: liability when workers know the land is not the hirer's

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when hired workers know they are digging on non-owned property and explain why liability falls on them.

Core Idea
Knowledge of invalidity eliminates deception, making workers directly liable.

This lesson covers the second scenario from al-Hidayah: when hired workers are aware that the land does not belong to the hirer. The ruling is that the workers themselves are liable. The reasoning is straightforward: the hirer's command is invalid because he has no ownership, and there is no deception (ghurur) to transfer the action. The workers' knowledge makes them responsible for their own voluntary act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the second ruling: 'If they knew that, then liability is on the workers.' Note the condition: workers have knowledge that the land is not the hirer's.
Knowledge is the key variable.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Two reasons given: (1) the hirer's command is not valid regarding something he does not own, so the command does not transfer liability; (2) there is no deception (ghurur) because the workers know the truth. Without deception, the action remains attributed to the workers.
No transfer of action occurs.
3
Contrast with the first scenario
Compare with the previous case: in the first scenario, the workers were deceived; here they are not. The distinction shows that liability hinges on the workers' state of knowledge.
Knowledge vs. ignorance changes the ruling.
4
Apply the principle
Conclude: when workers knowingly dig on non-owned property, they are liable for any harm because they acted with full awareness of the illegitimacy of the command.
Workers cannot shift liability.

مستاجر مزدوروں سے غیر فناء میں کنواں کھدوایا پھر کوئی مر گیا توضمان کس پر ہے

قال وإن استأجر أجراء فحفروها له في غير فنائه فذالك على المستأجر ولا شيء على الاجراء إن لم يعلموا أنها فى غير فنائه لأن الإجارة صحت ظاهرة إذا لم يعلموا فنقل فعلهم إليه لأنهم كانوا مغرورين فصار كما إذا أمر آخر بذبح هذه الشاة فذبحها ثم ظهر أن الشاة لغيره إلا أن هناك يضمن المأمور ويرجع على الآمر لأن الذابح مباشر والآمر مسبب والترجيح للمباشرة فيضمن ويرجع للغرور وهنا يجب الضمان على المستأجر ابتداء لأن كل واحد منهما مسبب والأجير غير متعد والمستأجر متعد فترجح جانبه

ترجمہ حضرت مصنف صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا اور اگر اس نے کچھ اجیر رکھے پس انہوں نے اس کے لئے ایک کنواں کھود دیا اس کی غیر فناء میں پس ضمان مستاجر پر ہوگا او مزدوروں پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اگر انہیں یہ بات معلوم نہ ہو کہ یہ کنواں کھودنا ) اس کی فناء کے غیر میں ہے اس لئے کہ اجارہ اس کے ظاہر کے اعتبار سے صحیح ہو گیا جب کہ انہیں علم نہ ہو تو ان کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ مستاجر کی جانب سے ) دھوکہ دیتے ہوئے ہیں پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی دوسر نے کسی شخص کو حکم کیا اس بکری کو ذبح کرنے کا پس اس نے اس کو ذبح کر دیا پھر یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ بکری اس کے غیر کی ہے مگر یہاں ( ذبیح کے مسئلہ میں ) مامور ( ذالخ ) ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح آمر کی جانب رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ ذابح مباشر ہے اور آمر مسبب ہے اور ترجیح مباشرت کو ہوتی ہے تو ذابح ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح دھو کہ کی وجہ سے آمر پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہاں ضمان پہلے ہی سے مستاجر پر واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مسبب ہے اور اجیر غیر متعدی ہے اور مستاجر متعدی ہے پس مستاجر کی جانب راجح ہو گئی۔

تشریح زید نے کچھ مزدوروں کو اجیر رکھا تا کہ فناء میں کنواں کھودیں انہوں نے کنواں کھودا اور اس کے اندر کوئی گر کر مر گیا، پہلے سے یہ بات مشہور نہ تھی کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے اب معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان کس پر واجب ہوگا ؟

تو فرمایا کہ صورت مذکورہ میں زید پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مزدوروں پر نہ ہو گا کیونکہ جب مزدوروں کو یہ علم نہیں ہے کہ یہ فنا کسی اور کی ہے بلکہ وہ اس کو زید کی فناء سمجھے ہوئے ہیں تو اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا اور جب اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا تو مزدوروں کا فعل مستاجر کی طرح منتقل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں زید ( مستاجر ) نے ان کو دھوکہ دیا ہے۔ اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کو حکم دیا کہ اس بکری کو ذبح کر دے اس نے ذبح کر دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بکری ساجد کی ہے تو یہاں ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اولا ضمان خالد پر واجب ہو گا اور پھر اس ضمان کو زید سے وصول کر لے گا۔ سوال یہاں اولا ضمان خالد پر کیوں واجب ہوا؟
جواب خالد چونکہ ڈائج ہے تو اس کا فعل مباشرت ہے اور زید نے حکم دیا ہے تو وہ فقط مسبب ہے اور مباشر ومسبب میں مباشر کوتر جیح ہوا کرتی ہے اس لئے خالد پر ضمان واجب ہوا لیکن چونکہ اس کو زید نے دھوکہ دیا ہے اس لئے خالد زید سے اس ضمان کو وصول کرے گا۔ سوال یہاں حفر بیر کے مسئلہ میں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے تھا کہ اولا ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوتا اور پھر مزدور اس کو مستاجر واپس لیتا؟
لجواب پہلے مسئلہ میں ذائع کو مباشر ہونے کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی تھی اور یہاں متاجر اور اجیر دونوں سب ہیں تو ترجیح کا مدار تعدی اور ظلم پر رہا اور تعدی صرف مستاجر کی طرف سے ہے اجیر کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔
اس لئے یہاں مستاجر کی جانب کو ترجیح دے کر اسی پر ضمان براہ راست واجب کر دیا۔

اگر ملک نہ ہونے کے علم کے باوجود کھودا تو مزدوروں پر ضمان ہے
وإن علموا ذالك فالضمان على الأجراء لأنه لم يصح أمره بما ليس بمملوك له ولا غرور فبقى الفعل مضافا إليهم.
ترجمہ اور اگر ان کو اس کا علم ہوتو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ مستاجر کا حکم اس چیز کے سلسلہ میں جو اس کی مملوک نہیں ہے اور دھو کہ دینا بھی نہیں ہے تو باقی بچا فعل مضاف انہیں کی طرف۔ تشریح اگر مزدوروں کو معلوم تھا کہ یہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں زید کا حکم صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ زید مالک نہیں ہے اور نہ یہاں زید نے دھوکہ دیا تو اس صورت میں یہ فعل مستاجر کی طرف مضاف نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اجراء کے اوپر ہی ضمان واجب ہوگا۔

مستاجر نے مزدوروں سے کہا کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں انہوں نے کھودا اور ایک آدمی اس میں مر گیا تو ضمان کس پر ہوگا
وإن قال لهم هذا فناى وليس لى فيه حق الحفر فحفروا فمات فيه إنسان فالضمان على الأجراء قياسا لأنهم علموا بفساد الأمر فما غرهم. وفى الاستحسان الضمان على المستأجر لأن كونه فناء له بمنزلة كونه مملوكا له لانطلاق يده فى التصرف فيه من إلقاء الطين والحطب وربط الدابة والركوب وبناء الدكان فكان الأمر بالحفر في ملكه ظاهرا بالنظر إلى ما ذكرنا فكفى ذالك لنقل الفعل إليه.

This is like if someone ordered another to slaughter this sheep and he slaughtered it, then it appeared that the sheep belonged to someone else—except that there the one ordered is liable and recovers from the orderer, because the slaughterer is the direct agent (mubashir) and the orderer is the indirect cause (musabbib), and preference is given to the direct agent, so he is liable and then recovers due to deception. Here, liability is imposed on the hirer from the beginning because each of them is an indirect cause, but the worker is not a transgressor (ghayr muta'addi) while the hirer is a transgressor (muta'addi), so his side is preponderant. 

If they knew that, then liability is on the workers because his command is not valid regarding something he does not own, and there is no deception, so the action remains attributed to them.

And if he said to them, 'This is my courtyard, but I have no right to dig in it,' and they dug, and a person died in it, then by analogy (qiyas) liability is on the workers because they knew the invalidity of the command, so he did not deceive them. Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the author (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) regarding liability when hired workers dig a well on land that turns out not to belong to the hirer. It covers three scenarios:
1) Workers unaware: The hirer is liable because the contract appeared valid and the workers were deceived. The action is attributed to the hirer as the indirect cause (musabbib) who is also a transgressor (muta'addi), while the workers are not transgressors. This is distinguished from the sheep slaughter analogy where the direct agent is liable first and then recovers from the orderer due to deception; here both are indirect causes, but the hirer's transgression tips the balance.
2) Workers aware: The hirer's command is invalid (he has no ownership), and there is no deception, so the workers are liable; their action is attributed to them.
3) Hirer says he has no right but workers dig: By qiyas, workers are liable because they knew the command was invalid. By istihsan, the hirer is liable because his de facto control over the courtyard (throwing dirt, etc.) makes it like his property, and the workers were not fully aware of the defect. The istihsan position is likely the relied-upon view, as it considers the practical authority of the hirer.

Key Terms
غرور (ghurur): Deception; leading someone to act based on a false appearance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Dispute: Qiyas vs. Istihsan When Hirer Disclaims Right to Dig
Third scenario: dispute between qiyas and istihsan when hirer disclaims right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute (qiyas vs. istihsan) in the case where the hirer says he has no right to dig but the workers dig anyway, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Even when the hirer admits no right, istihsan places liability on him due to apparent ownership.

This lesson examines the third scenario from al-Hidayah: the hirer tells the workers, 'This is my courtyard, but I have no right to dig in it.' The workers dig, and a person dies. The text presents two conflicting legal arguments: qiyas would make the workers liable because they knew the command was invalid; but istihsan makes the hirer liable because the courtyard is effectively his property due to his de facto control. The preferred view is istihsan, as it considers the hirer's apparent authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the third scenario: hirer says 'This is my courtyard, but I have no right to dig.' Workers dig nonetheless. A person dies. Note the ambiguity: workers know there is a problem, but the hirer still claims ownership.
Workers have partial knowledge (no right) but still rely on hirer's claim of ownership.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Qiyas (analogy) would hold workers liable because they knew the command was invalid (fasid). The reasoning: since they knew the hirer had no right, they were not deceived, so their action is attributed to them. This is similar to scenario 2.
Qiyas gives weight to the workers' knowledge of the invalidity.
3
Understand the istihsan argument
Istihsan (juristic preference) holds the hirer liable. The reasoning: the hirer's de facto control over the courtyard (throwing dirt, tying animals, etc.) makes it akin to his property. The command to dig is effectively a command in his own property, so the action is transferred to him regardless of his statement about rights.
Istihsan prioritizes apparent ownership and practical authority over technical invalidity.
4
Compare the two and identify the preferred view
The text presents qiyas first, then 'fi al-istihsan' (by istihsan) as the counter. Al-Marghinani likely prefers istihsan because it aligns with the principle that liability follows the one with greater control (the hirer) and protects workers who may be confused by the hirer's contradictory statement.
The preferred view is istihsan, making the hirer liable.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
Thus, in this scenario, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the hirer is liable, not the workers. The workers' partial knowledge does not shift liability because the hirer's apparent ownership overrides.
This is an exception to the rule that knowledge makes workers liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستاجر مزدوروں سے غیر فناء میں کنواں کھدوایا پھر کوئی مر گیا توضمان کس پر ہے

قال وإن استأجر أجراء فحفروها له في غير فنائه فذالك على المستأجر ولا شيء على الاجراء إن لم يعلموا أنها فى غير فنائه لأن الإجارة صحت ظاهرة إذا لم يعلموا فنقل فعلهم إليه لأنهم كانوا مغرورين فصار كما إذا أمر آخر بذبح هذه الشاة فذبحها ثم ظهر أن الشاة لغيره إلا أن هناك يضمن المأمور ويرجع على الآمر لأن الذابح مباشر والآمر مسبب والترجيح للمباشرة فيضمن ويرجع للغرور وهنا يجب الضمان على المستأجر ابتداء لأن كل واحد منهما مسبب والأجير غير متعد والمستأجر متعد فترجح جانبه

ترجمہ حضرت مصنف صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا اور اگر اس نے کچھ اجیر رکھے پس انہوں نے اس کے لئے ایک کنواں کھود دیا اس کی غیر فناء میں پس ضمان مستاجر پر ہوگا او مزدوروں پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اگر انہیں یہ بات معلوم نہ ہو کہ یہ کنواں کھودنا ) اس کی فناء کے غیر میں ہے اس لئے کہ اجارہ اس کے ظاہر کے اعتبار سے صحیح ہو گیا جب کہ انہیں علم نہ ہو تو ان کا فعل مستاجر کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ مستاجر کی جانب سے ) دھوکہ دیتے ہوئے ہیں پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی دوسر نے کسی شخص کو حکم کیا اس بکری کو ذبح کرنے کا پس اس نے اس کو ذبح کر دیا پھر یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ بکری اس کے غیر کی ہے مگر یہاں ( ذبیح کے مسئلہ میں ) مامور ( ذالخ ) ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح آمر کی جانب رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ ذابح مباشر ہے اور آمر مسبب ہے اور ترجیح مباشرت کو ہوتی ہے تو ذابح ضامن ہوگا اور ذابح دھو کہ کی وجہ سے آمر پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہاں ضمان پہلے ہی سے مستاجر پر واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مسبب ہے اور اجیر غیر متعدی ہے اور مستاجر متعدی ہے پس مستاجر کی جانب راجح ہو گئی۔

تشریح زید نے کچھ مزدوروں کو اجیر رکھا تا کہ فناء میں کنواں کھودیں انہوں نے کنواں کھودا اور اس کے اندر کوئی گر کر مر گیا، پہلے سے یہ بات مشہور نہ تھی کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے اب معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان کس پر واجب ہوگا ؟

تو فرمایا کہ صورت مذکورہ میں زید پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مزدوروں پر نہ ہو گا کیونکہ جب مزدوروں کو یہ علم نہیں ہے کہ یہ فنا کسی اور کی ہے بلکہ وہ اس کو زید کی فناء سمجھے ہوئے ہیں تو اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا اور جب اجارہ صحیح ہو گیا تو مزدوروں کا فعل مستاجر کی طرح منتقل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہاں زید ( مستاجر ) نے ان کو دھوکہ دیا ہے۔ اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کو حکم دیا کہ اس بکری کو ذبح کر دے اس نے ذبح کر دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بکری ساجد کی ہے تو یہاں ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اولا ضمان خالد پر واجب ہو گا اور پھر اس ضمان کو زید سے وصول کر لے گا۔ سوال یہاں اولا ضمان خالد پر کیوں واجب ہوا؟
جواب خالد چونکہ ڈائج ہے تو اس کا فعل مباشرت ہے اور زید نے حکم دیا ہے تو وہ فقط مسبب ہے اور مباشر ومسبب میں مباشر کوتر جیح ہوا کرتی ہے اس لئے خالد پر ضمان واجب ہوا لیکن چونکہ اس کو زید نے دھوکہ دیا ہے اس لئے خالد زید سے اس ضمان کو وصول کرے گا۔ سوال یہاں حفر بیر کے مسئلہ میں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے تھا کہ اولا ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوتا اور پھر مزدور اس کو مستاجر واپس لیتا؟
لجواب پہلے مسئلہ میں ذائع کو مباشر ہونے کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی تھی اور یہاں متاجر اور اجیر دونوں سب ہیں تو ترجیح کا مدار تعدی اور ظلم پر رہا اور تعدی صرف مستاجر کی طرف سے ہے اجیر کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔
اس لئے یہاں مستاجر کی جانب کو ترجیح دے کر اسی پر ضمان براہ راست واجب کر دیا۔

اگر ملک نہ ہونے کے علم کے باوجود کھودا تو مزدوروں پر ضمان ہے
وإن علموا ذالك فالضمان على الأجراء لأنه لم يصح أمره بما ليس بمملوك له ولا غرور فبقى الفعل مضافا إليهم.
ترجمہ اور اگر ان کو اس کا علم ہوتو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ مستاجر کا حکم اس چیز کے سلسلہ میں جو اس کی مملوک نہیں ہے اور دھو کہ دینا بھی نہیں ہے تو باقی بچا فعل مضاف انہیں کی طرف۔ تشریح اگر مزدوروں کو معلوم تھا کہ یہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں زید کا حکم صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ زید مالک نہیں ہے اور نہ یہاں زید نے دھوکہ دیا تو اس صورت میں یہ فعل مستاجر کی طرف مضاف نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اجراء کے اوپر ہی ضمان واجب ہوگا۔

مستاجر نے مزدوروں سے کہا کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں انہوں نے کھودا اور ایک آدمی اس میں مر گیا تو ضمان کس پر ہوگا
وإن قال لهم هذا فناى وليس لى فيه حق الحفر فحفروا فمات فيه إنسان فالضمان على الأجراء قياسا لأنهم علموا بفساد الأمر فما غرهم. وفى الاستحسان الضمان على المستأجر لأن كونه فناء له بمنزلة كونه مملوكا له لانطلاق يده فى التصرف فيه من إلقاء الطين والحطب وربط الدابة والركوب وبناء الدكان فكان الأمر بالحفر في ملكه ظاهرا بالنظر إلى ما ذكرنا فكفى ذالك لنقل الفعل إليه.
ترجمہ اور اگر مستاجر نے اجراء سے کہد یا ہو کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں ہے پس انہوں نے کھودا پس اس میں کوئی آدمی مر گیا تو قیا سا ضمان اجزاء پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان کو حکم کے فساد کا علم ہے تو مستاجر نے ان کو دھو کہ نہیں دیا
If he hired workers and they dug a well for him in his non-courtyard (property that is not his), then the liability is on the hirer (musta'jir) and nothing on the workers if they did not know that it was not in his courtyard, because the hire contract became valid on the face of it when they did not know, so their action is transferred to him because they were deceived. This is like if someone ordered another to slaughter this sheep and he slaughtered it, then it appeared that the sheep belonged to someone else—except that there the one ordered is liable and recovers from the orderer, because the slaughterer is the direct agent (mubashir) and the orderer is the indirect cause (musabbib), and preference is given to the direct agent, so he is liable and then recovers due to deception. Here, liability is imposed on the hirer from the beginning because each of them is an indirect cause, but the worker is not a transgressor (ghayr muta'addi) while the hirer is a transgressor (muta'addi), so his side is preponderant. 

If they knew that, then liability is on the workers because his command is not valid regarding something he does not own, and there is no deception, so the action remains attributed to them.

And if he said to them, 'This is my courtyard, but I have no right to dig in it,' and they dug, and a person died in it, then by analogy (qiyas) liability is on the workers because they knew the invalidity of the command, so he did not deceive them. But by juristic preference (istihsan), liability is on the hirer because his ownership of the courtyard is akin to ownership, due to his freedom of disposal—throwing dirt, firewood, tying an animal, riding, building a shop—so the command to dig in his property is apparent in view of what we mentioned, and that suffices to transfer the action to him.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the author (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) regarding liability when hired workers dig a well on land that turns out not to belong to the hirer. It covers three scenarios:
1) Workers unaware: The hirer is liable because the contract appeared valid and the workers were deceived. The action is attributed to the hirer as the indirect cause (musabbib) who is also a transgressor (muta'addi), while the workers are not transgressors. This is distinguished from the sheep slaughter analogy where the direct agent is liable first and then recovers from the orderer due to deception; here both are indirect causes, but the hirer's transgression tips the balance.
2) Workers aware: The hirer's command is invalid (he has no ownership), and there is no deception, so the workers are liable; their action is attributed to them.
3) Hirer says he has no right but workers dig: By qiyas, workers are liable because they knew the command was invalid. By istihsan, the hirer is liable because his de facto control over the courtyard (throwing dirt, etc.) makes it like his property, and the workers were not fully aware of the defect. The istihsan position is likely the relied-upon view, as it considers the practical authority of the hirer.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that abandons a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or subtle differences in the case.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; the application of a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario, what is the mufta bihi position regarding liability?
A) The workers are liable by qiyas
B) The hirer is liable by istihsan
C) Both are equally liable
D) No one is liable

Key Takeaway
Even when a hirer disclaims a right to dig, his de facto control over the property (as owner) makes him liable by istihsan, overriding the qiyas that would hold the workers liable.

Direct vs Indirect Cause in Liability: Mubashir and Mutasabbib
Explaining the rule of mubashir vs mutasabbib with an example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a direct cause (mubashir) and an indirect cause (mutasabbib) in Hanafi liability law, and apply the principle of preference based on transgression (ta'addi).

Core Idea
The direct agent is liable first, but transgression can shift liability to the indirect cause.

In Hanafi fiqh, when someone dies as a result of an act, the question arises: who bears the liability? Is it the person who directly performed the act, or the one who ordered it? This lesson explores a key example to demonstrate the principles of mubashir and mutasabbib, and how transgression can override the usual preference for the direct agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
In the example, Zaid orders Khalid to dig. Khalid is the direct agent (mubashir), Zaid is the indirect cause (mutasabbib).
2
Determine default liability
The default rule: the direct agent (mubashir) is liable first. Here, Khalid is initially liable.
3
Apply the exception for deception
Because Zaid deceived Khalid (by claiming the land was owned), Khalid recovers the liability from Zaid after paying.
Deception makes the indirect cause ultimately bear the loss.
4
Contrast with the well‑digging case
In a case where a hirer orders workers to dig, both are agents but the hirer is directly liable because the hirer alone transgresses (ta'addi) by ordering the dig on another's land.
When both are agents, transgression determines liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہاں ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اولا ضمان خالد پر واجب ہو گا اور پھر اس ضمان کو زید سے وصول کر لے گا۔ سوال یہاں اولا ضمان خالد پر کیوں واجب ہوا؟
جواب خالد چونکہ ڈائج ہے تو اس کا فعل مباشرت ہے اور زید نے حکم دیا ہے تو وہ فقط مسبب ہے اور مباشر ومسبب میں مباشر کوتر جیح ہوا کرتی ہے اس لئے خالد پر ضمان واجب ہوا لیکن چونکہ اس کو زید نے دھوکہ دیا ہے اس لئے خالد زید سے اس ضمان کو وصول کرے گا۔ سوال یہاں حفر بیر کے مسئلہ میں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہیئے تھا کہ اولا ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوتا اور پھر مزدور اس کو مستاجر واپس لیتا؟
لجواب پہلے مسئلہ میں ذائع کو مباشر ہونے کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی تھی اور یہاں متاجر اور اجیر دونوں سب ہیں تو ترجیح کا مدار تعدی اور ظلم پر رہا اور تعدی صرف مستاجر کی طرف سے ہے اجیر کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں مستاجر کی جانب کو ترجیح دے کر اسی پر ضمان براہ راست واجب کر دیا۔
Here liability is obligatory. First, liability is upon Khalid, and then he will recover that liability from Zaid. Question: Why is liability first upon Khalid? Answer: Because Khalid is the digger, his act is direct, and Zaid only gave the command, so he is merely a cause. And between the direct and the indirect, the direct is given preference. Therefore liability is upon Khalid, but since Zaid deceived him, Khalid will recover this liability from Zaid. Question: In the well-digging issue, should it not have been similar, that liability would first be upon the workers and then the workers would take it back from the hirer? Answer: In the first issue, we gave preference to the direct agent due to being direct. Here, the hirer and the worker are both agents, so the basis of preference is transgression and injustice, and transgression is only from the side of the hirer, not from the worker. Therefore, here, giving preference to the hirer's side, liability was made directly upon him.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the distinction between a direct cause (mubashir) and an indirect cause (mutasabbib) in liability for death. The scenario involves Zaid ordering Khalid to dig a well on land that is not owned by Zaid, and a man dies. The ruling states that Khalid, as the direct agent, is first liable, but because Zaid deceived him (by leading him to believe the land was owned), Khalid can recover from Zaid. The text then addresses a question about a different scenario: in the well-digging case where a hirer (mu'ajjir) hires workers (ujara') to dig, why is the liability directly on the hirer and not first on the workers? The answer is that in the first scenario, the direct cause (Khalid) was given preference because he was the direct agent. But here both the hirer and the worker are agents; the decisive factor is transgression (ta'addi). The hirer alone transgresses by ordering the dig, while the workers merely follow orders without transgression. Therefore, liability is placed directly on the hirer. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the attributive factor in liability is not merely direct causation but the presence of transgression and injustice.

Key Terms
مباشر (mubāshir): The one who directly performs the act causing death, e.g., the digger.
مسبب (mutasabbib): The one who indirectly causes the act through command or deception, e.g., the person who ordered the digging.
تعدی (ta‘addī): Transgression or exceeding legal limits; the basis for preferring one party's liability over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where Zaid orders Khalid to dig a well on land not owned by Zaid, and a man dies, who is initially liable?
A) Zaid, because he gave the order
B) Khalid, because he is the direct agent
C) Both are equally liable
D) Neither, because the victim was negligent

Key Takeaway
Liability is initially on the direct agent, but transgression or deception can shift it to the indirect cause.

Liability of Laborers When They Know the Land Is Not Owned
Ruling when laborers know land is not owned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability of workers when they know the land is not owned and explain the reasoning based on invalid command and absence of deception.

Core Idea
When workers know the land is not owned, they are liable because the command is invalid and there is no deception.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in liability (diyat) where hired workers dig land that does not belong to the hirer. The key factor is the workers' knowledge: if they know the land is not owned, the hirer's command is invalid and there is no deception, so the act is attributed to the workers, making them liable. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that liability follows the one who has control and knowledge, not merely the one who gives an invalid command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage to recognize the specific case: hired workers dig land not owned by the hirer. The text distinguishes between workers who know and those who do not know the land's status.
Focus on the condition of knowledge.
2
Determine the ruling
State the explicit ruling: if workers know the land is not owned, liability is on them (the workers). This is the Hanafi position.
Liability here means they must pay compensation (diyah) if death occurs.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is twofold: (1) the hirer's command is invalid because he has no ownership over the land, so his command carries no authority; (2) there is no deception (ghurur) from the hirer since the workers are aware of the truth. Hence, the act of digging is solely attributed to the workers.
Invalid command + no deception = act attributed to workers.
4
Contrast with the opposite scenario
If the workers are unaware, the hirer's command may be valid due to apparent authority, and deception may exist, making the hirer liable. This is implied but not detailed in this passage.
Knowledge shifts liability.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools hold the hirer liable regardless of the workers' knowledge because the command initiated the act. Recognize this as a valid ikhtilaf.
Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

اگر ملک نہ ہونے کے علم کے باوجود کھودا تو مزدوروں پر ضمان ہے
وإن علموا ذالك فالضمان على الأجراء لأنه لم يصح أمره بما ليس بمملوك له ولا غرور فبقى الفعل مضافا إليهم.
ترجمہ اور اگر ان کو اس کا علم ہوتو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ مستاجر کا حکم اس چیز کے سلسلہ میں جو اس کی مملوک نہیں ہے اور دھو کہ دینا بھی نہیں ہے تو باقی بچا فعل مضاف انہیں کی طرف۔ تشریح اگر مزدوروں کو معلوم تھا کہ یہ زید کی فنا نہیں ہے تو ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں زید کا حکم صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ زید مالک نہیں ہے اور نہ یہاں زید نے دھوکہ دیا تو اس صورت میں یہ فعل مستاجر کی طرف مضاف نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا اجراء کے اوپر ہی ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
If they dug despite knowing the lack of ownership, then liability is on the workers. And if they knew that, then liability is on the workers because his command is not valid regarding what is not owned by him, and there is no deception, so the act remains attributed to them. Translation: And if they had knowledge of that, then liability is obligatory upon the workers because the hirer's command is not valid concerning something he does not own, and there is no deception, so the act remains attributed to them. Explanation: If the workers knew that this was not Zaid's forecourt, then liability is upon the workers because Zaid's command is not valid, as Zaid is not the owner, and Zaid did not deceive them. In that case, the act is not attributed to the hirer, so liability is upon the workers.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing a specific sub-case: what happens when the workers (ujara') know that the land being dug is not owned by the hirer (mu'ajjir). The ruling states that if the workers have knowledge of this fact, then they are liable for any death resulting from the digging, not the hirer. The proof given is that the hirer's command is invalid because he has no ownership or authority over the land (since it is not his property). Furthermore, there is no deception (ghurur) from the hirer, because the workers are aware of the situation. Consequently, the act of digging is attributed solely to the workers themselves, as they acted with knowledge and without inducement. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that liability follows the one who has both knowledge and control over the act.

Key Terms
غرور (ghurūr): Deception; leading someone to believe something false. Absence of deception shifts liability to the actor.
أجراء (ujarā’): Plural of ajir; hired workers/laborers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The hirer
B) The workers
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
When workers have knowledge of the illegitimacy of the hirer's command, liability shifts to them due to valid attribution and absence of deception.

Applying Qiyas and Istihsan to Liability in a Forecourt
Comparison of qiyas and istihsan for liability in a forecourt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas in liability for digging in a forecourt, and identify the basis for the preferred ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan can override qiyas when the apparent ownership of the forecourt transfers liability to the hirer.

Consider a hirer who tells workers to dig a well in his forecourt, admitting he has no right to dig. The workers dig, and a man falls in and dies. Who is liable? The answer depends on whether we apply strict analogy (qiyas) or juristic preference (istihsan). This passage from Al-Hidayah presents both approaches and shows why the Hanafi school chooses istihsan. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi method of legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Legal Question
Read the passage carefully. The hirer (musta'jir) tells workers that the forecourt is his but he has no right to dig. The workers dig anyway, and a man dies. The question: who is liable (daman)?
The forecourt (fana') is a semi-public space customarily used by the householder.
2
Understand the Qiyas Ruling and Its Rationale
By qiyas, liability falls on the workers. Why? Because they knew the hirer's command was invalid (he had no right to dig), so they acted on their own risk. The hirer did not deceive them (ghurur). The illa (effective cause) is their knowledge of the invalidity of the command.
This is the straightforward analogy from cases where agents knowingly act under an invalid order.
3
Understand the Istihsan Ruling and Its Basis
By istihsan, liability shifts to the hirer. Why? Because the forecourt, due to the hirer's extensive usage (throwing mud, tying animals, etc.), appears to be his property. Therefore, his command to dig seems to be within his property, making the workers' act attributable to him.
Istihsan here considers the public perception and customary practice, overriding strict qiyas.
4
Grasp Why Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
The Hanafi school holds that the apparent ownership (milk zahir) suffices to transfer liability. The workers are not at fault because they reasonably believed the hirer had authority over the forecourt. Istihsan gives weight to custom (urf) and the apparent state of affairs.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that istihsan can override qiyas when there is a stronger countervailing consideration.
5
Note the Practical Outcome and Hanafi Preference
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the hirer is liable. This has practical implications: for example, if a similar incident occurs in a public pathway where a shopkeeper customarily stores goods, the shopkeeper would be liable, not the workers.
Other schools may follow qiyas and hold the workers liable. The Hanafi stance is based on custom and apparent authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستاجر نے مزدوروں سے کہا کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں
انہوں نے کھودا اور ایک آدمی اس میں مر گیا تو ضمان کس پر ہوگا
وإن قال لهم هذا فناى وليس لى فيه حق الحفر فحفروا فمات فيه إنسان فالضمان على الأجراء قياسا لأنهم علموا بفساد الأمر فما غرهم. وفى الاستحسان الضمان على المستأجر لأن كونه فناء له بمنزلة كونه مملوكا له لانطلاق يده فى التصرف فيه من إلقاء الطين والحطب وربط الدابة والركوب وبناء الدكان فكان الأمر بالحفر في ملكه ظاهرا بالنظر إلى ما ذكرنا فكفى ذالك لنقل الفعل إليه. ترجمہ اور اگر مستاجر نے اجراء سے کہد یا ہو کہ یہ میری فناء ہے اور مجھے اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں ہے پس انہوں نے کھودا پس اس میں کوئی آدمی مر گیا تو قیا سا ضمان اجزاء پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان کو حکم کے فساد کا علم ہے تو مستاجر نے ان کو دھو کہ نہیں دیا ہے اور استحسان میں مستاجر پر ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کا متاجر کے لئے فناء ہونا اس کے مملوک ہونے کے درجہ میں ہے اس میں تصرف میں اس کے قبضہ کے جاری ہونے کی وجہ سے یعنی مٹی ڈالنا، اور ایندھن ڈالنا اور چوپایہ باندھنا اور سوار ہونا اور چبوترہ بنانا تو کھودنے کا حکم ظاہری طور پر اپنی ملک میں ہوا ، ان چیزوں کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہیں۔ پس مستاجر کی جانب فعل منتقل کرنے کے لئے اتنی سی بات کافی ہے۔
تشریح اگر وہ جگہ ہے تو زید کے ھر یا فناء میں جو اس کے استعمال میں ہے وہاں کبھی چارپائی بچھاتا ہے، چوپائے باندھتا ہے، ہنی ڈالتا ہے اور اپنا ایندھن ڈالتا ہے چبوترہ بناتا ہے۔ وہاں سوار ہو کر آتا جاتا ہے لیکن اس کو اس میں کنواں کھودنے کا حق نہیں ہے جیسے جہاں بستیوں میں سڑک نکلی ہوئی ہیں تو سڑک کے اطراف کی زمین اگر چہ اطراف میں گھر والے اپنے ان سب استعمالوں میں اس کی لیتے ہیں مگر زمین کے وہ مالک نہیں ہوتے اگر ایسی جگہ زید کے کہنے سے مزدوروں نے کنواں کھودا اور زید نے مزدوروں کو بتا بھی دیا کہ اس فناء کی پوزیشن یہ ہے پھر اس میں کوئی شخص گر کر ہلاک ہو گیا تو اب ضمان کس پر واجب ہوگا۔ تو قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ ضمان مزدوروں پر واجب ہو کیونکہ یہاں زید نے ان کو کوئی دھوکہ نہیں دیا۔ بات کو صاف بتا دیا اور ان کو بھی حکم کے فساد کا علم ہے تو مجرم یہی ہوئے لہذا انہیں پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
مگر قیاس کو چھوڑ کر استحسان کا تقاضہ یہ ہوا کہ ضمان مستاجر پر ہوگا کیونکہ مذکورہ تصرفات کے حق کی وجہ سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ فناء زید کی ہی مملوک ہے، اور بلحاظ ظا ہر ا تنا حق تصرف اس بات کے لئے کافی ہے کہ مزدوروں کا فعل متاجر کی طرف منتقل کر دیا جائے۔
The hirer said to the workers: 'This is my forecourt, and I have no right to dig in it.' They dug, and a man died in it. Who is liable? And if he said to them: 'This is my forecourt, and I have no right to dig in it,' so they dug and a man died in it, then by qiyas liability is on the workers because they knew the command was invalid, so he did not deceive them. And by istihsan liability is on the hirer because his forecourt is in the position of being owned by him due to the free use of his hand in disposing of it, such as throwing mud, firewood, tying animals, riding, and building a shop. So the order to dig was apparently in his property, considering what we mentioned. That suffices to transfer the act to him. Translation and explanation follow.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof involving a dispute between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) within the Hanafi school. The scenario: a hirer (musta'jir) tells workers that this is his forecourt (fana') but he has no right to dig a well. The workers dig anyway, and a man dies. By qiyas, the workers are liable because they knew the command was invalid (the hirer had no right to dig), and there was no deception (ghurur) from the hirer. However, by istihsan, the hirer is liable because the forecourt appears to be his property due to his extensive use (e.g., throwing mud, tying animals, etc.), so the command to dig appears to be within his property, thus transferring the act to him. The commentary explains that qiyas would place liability on the workers, but following istihsan, the preferred ruling is that the hirer is liable. This illustrates a key Hanafi method: istihsan can override qiyas when there is a compelling reason based on custom or apparent ownership.

Key Terms
فناء (fanā’): Forecourt or open space adjacent to a house, used by the owner for various purposes like storing items, tying animals, etc.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of overriding qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or hidden analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hirer is liable by istihsan

D) Both are jointly liable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers istihsan over qiyas in determining liability for digging in a forecourt because the hirer's apparent ownership transfers the act to him.
