امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل:
وله أن المسجد بني للصلاة وهذه الأشياء ملحقة بها فلابد من إظهار التفاوت فجعلنا الجلوس للأصل
A person from the people of the mosque was sitting in the mosque and another person died because of him; is there liability on the sitter or not, whether the sitter is in prayer or not? Statements of the jurists: He (Muhammad) said: And if a man from them sat in it and a man was killed because of him, he is not liable if he was in prayer, and if he was not in prayer he is liable, and this is according to Abu Hanifa; and they (Sahibayn) said he is not liable in any case. And if he is sitting for recitation of Quran, or for teaching, or for prayer, or he slept in it during prayer, or slept outside prayer, or a passerby passed through, or sat for conversation, then it is upon this difference. And as for one in i'tikaf, it has been said it is upon this difference, and it has been said he is not liable by consensus. Translation: Muhammad said: And if a man among them (from the people of the mosque) sat in the mosque and a person died because of him, then if he was in prayer, he is not liable, and if he was not in prayer, he is liable, and this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa; and the two companions said: he is not liable in any case. And if he is sitting for recitation of Quran, or for teaching, or for prayer (waiting), or he slept in the mosque during prayer, or slept outside prayer, or a passerby passed through the mosque, or sat for conversation, then it is upon this difference. And as for the mu'takif: it has been said it is upon this difference, and it has been said he is not liable by consensus. Explanation: A person from the people of the mosque is sitting in the mosque and someone slips and dies because of him; is there liability? He said: If that person is in prayer, by consensus he is not liable; if he is not in prayer, then there is a difference: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, liability is wajib; according to Sahibayn, liability is not wajib. And when he is not in prayer, the author (Muhammad) mentioned seven scenarios: (1) sitting for recitation of Quran, (2) sitting for fiqh or hadith, (3) sitting waiting for prayer, (4) he was praying and fell asleep during prayer, (5) he fell asleep outside of prayer, (6) he was passing through the mosque when someone died because of him, (7) he sat in the mosque for conversation. And if a mu'takif is sitting and someone collides with him and dies, there are two sayings: this is also a disputed issue, or it is consensual – there is no liability. Caution: The one waiting for prayer is not liable, even according to Imam Abu Hanifa. (From Shami, vol.5, p.382) The proof of the two companions: For them is that the mosque was built only for prayer and dhikr, and he cannot perform prayer in congregation except by waiting for it, so sitting in it is permissible because it is from the necessities of prayer, or because the one waiting for prayer is in prayer by ruling according to the hadith, so he is not liable just as when he is in prayer. Translation: The proof of Sahibayn is that the mosque was built for prayer and dhikr, and performing congregational prayer is not possible without waiting for the congregation, so sitting in the mosque is permissible because it is from the necessities of prayer, or because the one waiting for prayer is by the hadith considered in a state of prayer, so he should not be liable just as when he is in prayer. Explanation: In this disputed issue, this is the proof of Sahibayn: they say that the mosque was built so that prayer be performed in it and Allah be remembered. And when one performs congregational prayer, some waiting is necessary, so sitting in the mosque is also permissible because sitting in the mosque is from the necessities of prayer. Also, if he is in prayer, by consensus there is no liability, but the hadith states that the one waiting for prayer is also in prayer by ruling, and when he is in prayer, liability should not be incurred. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: And for him is that the mosque was built for prayer, and these things are attached to it, so it is necessary to show a distinction, so we make sitting for the original [purpose] [exempt]...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability (daman) when a person sitting in a mosque causes harm to another, such as causing them to fall and die. The ruling from Imam Muhammad (the matn) states: if the sitter is in prayer, there is no liability by consensus; if not in prayer, Abu Hanifa holds liability, while Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold no liability in all cases. The commentary then lists seven scenarios of being in the mosque without prayer: reciting Quran, teaching, waiting for prayer, sleeping during prayer, sleeping outside prayer, passing through, and sitting for conversation. All these fall under the same dispute. The mu'takif (one in i'tikaf) has two reports: one on the same dispute, another of no liability by consensus. Sahibayn's proof relies on the purpose of the mosque (prayer and dhikr) and the hadith that the one waiting for prayer is considered in prayer, thus exempt from liability. Abu Hanifa's proof (partially given) argues that the mosque was built specifically for prayer, and other activities are merely attached; therefore a distinction must be made, exempting only sitting for the original purpose (prayer).

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for harm caused; here, specifically for death caused by one's sitting.
منتظر الصلاة (muntazir al-salah): One who sits in the mosque waiting for the congregational prayer to begin.
معتکف (mu'takif): One who performs i'tikaf (spiritual retreat) in the mosque, staying for a defined period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about the liability for harm caused by a sitter in the mosque?
A) Both Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn agree that there is no liability if the sitter is in prayer.
B) Abu Hanifa holds that there is liability even if the sitter is in prayer.
C) Sahibayn hold that there is liability only if the sitter is not in prayer.
D) All scenarios of non-prayer sitting are exempt by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The liability of a sitter in the mosque for accidental harm depends on his activity: unanimous exemption for prayer itself; for non-prayer, Abu Hanifa imposes liability while Sahibayn exempt, except that waiting for prayer is exempt even by Abu Hanifa.

intermediate

Liability for Sitting in Mosque: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for sitting in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for death caused by sitting in a mosque, state Abu Hanifa's distinction between mubah mutlaq and mubah muqayyad, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
In the mosque, sitting for prayer itself is unconditionally permissible; sitting for attached acts is conditioned on safety.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The question is: if a person sitting in a mosque accidentally causes someone's death (e.g., by tripping), is he liable for blood money (diyah)? The answer depends on whether the sitting is for the original purpose of prayer or for an attached act like waiting. Abu Hanifa introduces a subtle distinction in types of permissibility, while the Sahibayn treat waiting as legally equivalent to prayer. This dispute reveals how the Hanafi school navigates between absolute permission and accountability.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify that Abu Hanifa distinguishes between sitting for the original act of prayer (absolutely permissible, mubah mutlaq) and sitting for attached acts like waiting (permissible only with condition of safety, mubah muqayyad). Only the latter can incur liability.
The original act is the prayer itself; attached acts include waiting, studying, etc.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
The Sahibayn hold that whoever sits in the mosque for a purpose connected to prayer (especially waiting for congregation) is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer and remembrance, and waiting is a necessity for congregational prayer.
They also invoke the hadith that the one waiting for prayer is legally considered in prayer.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Their dalil: the mosque is built for prayer; congregational prayer requires waiting; thus sitting for waiting is permissible as a necessity. Additionally, the hadith 'the one waiting for prayer is in prayer' extends the immunity from liability enjoyed by one actually praying.
This is a qiyas based on the hadith's legal implication.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa responds that the hadith yields a legal ruling (hukman) but not identity in all respects. He insists on showing a distinction (tafawut) between the original and the attached. He supports with analogies: shooting at an enemy (recommended but liable if it hits a Muslim), walking (mubah but liable if stepping on someone), sleeping in mosque (mubah but liable if rolling over another).
These analogies show that even recommended or permissible acts can be conditioned on safety.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical consequence: according to Sahibayn, the waiting person is never liable; according to Abu Hanifa, he may be liable if harm occurs. The text later notes (from Shami) that even Abu Hanifa said the one waiting is not liable, indicating a potential reconciliation or the operative fatwa.
The mufta bihi may be that waiting for prayer does not incur liability, but the principle of mubah muqayyad remains important for other attached acts.

صاحبین کی دلیل
لهما أن المسجد إنما بنى للصلاة والذكر ولا يمكنه أداء الصلاة بالجماعة إلا بانتظارها فكان الجلوس فيه مباحا لأنه من ضرورات الصلاة أو لأن المنتظر للصلاة في الصلاة حكما بالحديث فلايضمن كما إذا كان في الصلاة
ترجمہ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسجد نماز اور ذکر کرنے کے لئے بنائی گئی ہے اور اس کو جماعت سے نماز پڑھنا بغیر جماعت کے انتظار ممکن نہیں تو اس میں جلوس مباح ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہ جلوس نماز کی ضروریات میں سے ہے یا اس لئے کہ نماز کا انتظار کرنے والا حدیث کی وجہ سے حکماً نماز میں ہے تو وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے جب کہ وہ نماز میں ہو۔ تشریح اختلافی مسئلہ میں یہ صاحبین کی دلیل ہے، کہتے ہیں کہ مسجد اس لئے بنائی جاتی ہے کہ اس میں نماز پڑھی جائے اور اللہ کا ذکر کیا جائے۔ اور جب جماعت کی نماز ادا کرے گا تو کچھ انتظار کرنا پڑے گا تو مسجد میں بیٹھنا بھی مباح ہوگا کیونکہ مسجد میں بیٹھنا ضروریات صلوة میں سے ہے، نیز اگر وہ نماز میں ہو تو بالا تفاق ضمان نہیں ہے لیکن حدیث میں آگیا کہ نماز کا انتظار کرنے والا بھی حکما نماز میں ہے اور جب وہ نماز میں ہے تو ضمان نہ ہونا چاہیئے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل
وله أن المسجد بني للصلاة وهذه الأشياء ملحقة بها فلابد من إظهار التفاوت فجعلنا الجلوس للأصل مباحا مطلقا والجلوس لما يلحق به مباحا مقيدا بشرط السلامة ولا غرو أن يكون الفعل مباحا أو مندوبا إليه وهو مقيد بشرط السلامة كالرمى إلى الكافر أو إلى الصيد والمشى فى الطريق والمشى في المسجد إذا وطىء غيره والنوم فيه إذا انقلب على غيره.
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسجد نماز کے لئے بنائی گئی ہے اور یہ تمام چیزیں نماز کے ساتھ ملحق ہیں تو تفاوت کو ظاہر کرنا ضروری ہے تو ہم نے اصل کے لئے جلوس کو مطلقاً مباح کر دیا اور اس کام کے لئے جو اصل کے ساتھ ملحق ہیں ایسا مباح کر دیا جو سلامتی کی شرط کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور یہ کوئی تعجب کی بات نہیں کہ ایک کام مباح یا مندوب ہو حالانکہ وہ سلامتی کی شرط کے ساتھ مقید ہو۔ جیسے کافر کی طرف تیر پھینکنا یا شکار کی طرف اور راستہ میں چلنا اور مسجد میں چلنا جب کہ وہ اپنے غیر پر پلٹ جائے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے مسجد کی بناء نماز کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔ اور باقی امور مذکورہ نماز نہیں بلکہ ملحق بالصلوۃ ہیں تو نماز اور غیر نماز میں فرق کرنا ضروری ہو تو ہم نے کہا کہ نماز کے لئے جلوس ضمان کا باعث نہیں کیونکہ یہ مطلقاً مباح ہے وصف سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے اور ملحقات کے لئے جلوس مباح مقید ہے لہذا شرط سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید رہے گا۔ اور ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ کوئی کام مباح ہے بلکہ مندوب ہے اس کے باوجود بھی وصف سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید ہے جیسے کافر کی طرف تیر پھینکنا مندوب ہے لیکن اگر کسی مسلمان کو لگ گیا تو اس کا ضمان واجب ہوگا اور شکار کرنا مباح ہے لہذا اگر اس کو تیر مارتے ہوئے اور کولگ گیا تو مهمان واجب ہو گا ایسے ہی راستہ میں چلنا اور مسجد میں چلنا مباح ہے۔ لیکن اگر اپنے پاؤں سے کسی کو روند دیا تو ضمان ادا کرنا ہوگا، اسی طرح مسافر ومختلف کے لئے مسجد میں سونا مباح ہے لیکن سوتے ہوئے اگر کسی کے اوپر پلٹ گیا اور وہ مر گیا تو ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
اسی طرح راستہ میں اصلاح ذات البین کے لئے بیٹھنا قربت ہے لیکن اگر اس سے کوئی چیز ضائع ہو جائے تو ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ ملاحظہ ہو زیلعی
اہل مسجد کے علاوہ کوئی شخص مسجد میں بیٹھا نماز پڑھ رہاتھا کہ کوئی شخص ہلاک ہو گیا بیٹھنے والا ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں
وإن جلس رجل من غير العشيرة فيه فى الصلاة فتعقل به إنسان ينبغى أن لا يضمن لأن المسجد بني للصلاة وأمر الصلاة بالجماعة إن كان مفوضا إلى أهل المسجد فلكل واحد من المسلمين أن يصلى فيه وحده
ترجمہ. اور اگر اہل مسجد کے غیر میں سے کوئی شخص مسجد میں بیٹھا ہو نماز میں پس اس سے کوئی انسان پھسل گیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ وہ ضامن نہ ہو اس لئے کہ مسجد نماز کے لئے بنائی گئی ہے اور نماز با جماعت کا کام ( نظم ) اگر چہ اہل مسجد کے سپرد ہے پس ہر مسلمان کے لئے یہ تو حق ہے کہ اس میں تنہا نماز پڑھے۔ تشریح کوئی دوسرا شخص جو اہل محلہ میں سے نہیں ہے مسجد میں نماز میں بیٹھا ہوا ہے جس کی وجہ سے کوئی پھسل کر مر گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہ ہو
The commentary mentions: The one sitting for recitation of Quran, for fiqh or hadith, waiting for prayer, praying and then fell asleep in prayer, fell asleep outside prayer, passing through the mosque and someone dies due to him, or sitting for conversation. And if a mu'takif is sitting and someone collides with him and dies, there are two sayings. This is also a disputed issue. It is consensus that there is no liability. Note: The one waiting for prayer will not be liable, even according to Imam Abu Hanifa. (Shami vol. 5 p. 382). The proof of the Sahibayn: For them, the mosque is built for prayer and remembrance, and one cannot perform prayer in congregation without waiting, so sitting in it is permissible because it is from the necessities of prayer, or because the one waiting for prayer is, by virtue of a hadith, legally in prayer, so he is not liable just as if he were in prayer. Translation: The proof of the Sahibayn is that the mosque is built for prayer and remembrance, and performing prayer in congregation is not possible without waiting, so sitting in it is permissible because it is from the necessities of prayer, or because the one waiting for prayer is by virtue of a hadith legally in prayer, so he is not liable, like when he is in prayer. Explanation: In this disputed issue, this is the proof of the Sahibayn: they say the mosque is built so that prayer is offered in it and Allah is remembered. And when one performs congregational prayer, some waiting is necessary, so sitting in the mosque is permissible because it is from the necessities of prayer. Also, if he were in prayer, there is no liability by agreement, but the hadith says that the one waiting for prayer is legally in prayer, so when he is in prayer, there should be no liability. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: And for him, the mosque is built for prayer, and these things are attached to it, so it is necessary to show the distinction. So we made sitting for the original act absolutely permissible, and sitting for what is attached to it permissible but conditioned on safety. And it is not strange that an act is permissible or recommended while it is conditioned on safety, like shooting at a disbeliever or at game, walking on the road, and walking in the mosque if he steps on someone, and sleeping in it if he rolls over someone. Translation: And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that the mosque is built for prayer, and all these things are attached to prayer, so it is necessary to show the difference. So we made sitting for the original act absolutely permissible, and for the act attached to the original, we made it permissible but conditioned on safety. And it is not strange that an act is permissible or recommended while it is conditioned on safety, like shooting an arrow at a disbeliever or at game, walking on the road, and walking in the mosque when he steps on someone else. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. The building of the mosque is for prayer, and the other mentioned matters are not prayer but attached to prayer. So it is necessary to differentiate between prayer and non-prayer. So we said that sitting for prayer does not cause liability because it is absolutely permissible, not conditioned on safety, and sitting for attached matters is permissible but conditioned, so it remains conditioned on safety. And it happens that an act is permissible or even recommended yet it is conditioned on safety, like shooting an arrow at a disbeliever is recommended, but if it hits a Muslim, liability becomes wajib; hunting is permissible, so if while shooting an arrow it hits someone else, liability becomes wajib; similarly walking on the road and walking in the mosque are permissible, but if one's foot tramples someone, one must pay liability; similarly sleeping in the mosque for a traveler is permissible, but if while sleeping one rolls over someone and they die, liability becomes wajib. Similarly, sitting on the road for reconciliation between people is an act of closeness, but if something is lost due to it, liability becomes wajib. See Zaylai. A person other than the residents of the mosque sitting in prayer in the mosque, and a person dies, will the sitter be liable or not? And if a man from other than the residents sits in it in prayer, and a person stumbles over him, it should be that he is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer, and the matter of congregational prayer, though entrusted to the residents of the mosque, every Muslim has the right to pray in it alone. Translation: And if a person other than the residents sits in the mosque in prayer, and a person slips due to him, then it is appropriate that he is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer, and the arrangement of congregational prayer, though entrusted to the residents, every Muslim has the right to pray alone in it. Explanation: Another person who is not from the residents of the locality is sitting in the mosque in prayer, due to which someone slips and dies; he will not be liable.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute about liability (daman) for accidental death caused by a person sitting in a mosque. The author lists several scenarios: sitting for Quran recitation, for fiqh/hadith study, waiting for prayer, praying then sleeping in prayer, sleeping outside prayer, passing through, and sitting for conversation. The central dispute concerns the person waiting for prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that such a person is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer and remembrance, and waiting is a necessity of congregational prayer. Moreover, a hadith states that the one waiting for prayer is legally considered to be in prayer, and one in prayer is not liable. Imam Abu Hanifa differentiates: sitting for the original purpose (prayer itself) is absolutely permissible (mubah mutlaq) and does not require a condition of safety, so it incurs no liability. However, sitting for acts attached to prayer (like waiting, studying, etc.) is permissible but conditioned on safety (mubah muqayyad bi shart al-salamah). Therefore, if someone dies due to such sitting, liability arises unless it was for the original act of prayer. Abu Hanifa illustrates with analogies: shooting at an enemy or game is permissible/recommended but if it hits a Muslim, liability applies; walking on the road is permissible but if you trample someone, liability applies; sleeping in the mosque is permissible for a traveler but if you roll over someone, liability applies. The passage concludes with a scenario: if a person not from the local residents sits in the mosque performing prayer (i.e., the original act), and someone slips and dies, the sitter is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer and everyone has the right to pray there.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): The legal liability to pay compensation for harm or death caused.
مطلقاً مباح (mutlaqan mubah): Permissible without any restrictive condition, especially regarding liability.
مباح مقید بشرط السلامة (mubah muqayyad bi shart al-salamah): Permissible but conditioned on ensuring safety of others; if harm occurs, liability arises.
انتظار الصلاة (intizar al-salah): Waiting for the congregational prayer in the mosque.
ملحق بالصلاة (mulhaq bi al-salah): Acts that are attached or ancillary to prayer, such as waiting, studying, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the status of sitting in a mosque for the purpose of waiting for congregation prayer?
A) It is absolutely permissible (mubah mutlaq) and incurs no liability.
B) It is permissible but conditioned on safety (mubah muqayyad bi shart al-salamah), so if someone dies, liability may arise.
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is recommended (mustahab) unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's distinction between mubah mutlaq and mubah muqayyad is key to determining liability for acts in the mosque, with the original prayer being unconditionally safe and attached acts conditioned on safety.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
6 min
Liability of a Non-Resident Praying in a Mosque
Ruling with proof on liability for harm caused by permissible act in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a non-resident praying in a mosque is not liable for accidental harm caused by their presence, and explain the role of transgression (ta'addi) in liability.

Core Idea
A permissible act without transgression does not create liability, even if harm occurs incidentally.

In the Hanafi school, liability for accidental harm hinges on whether the act was transgressive (mut'addi). This lesson examines a case where a non-local sits in a mosque to pray, and someone trips over him. The ruling is clear: no compensation is due. Why? Because the act of praying in a mosque is permissible for every Muslim, and the person was not a trespasser. Let's unpack the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Pinpoint the specific situation: a man from outside the local community sits in a mosque in prayer, and someone is tripped by him (e.g., slips and dies).
The key is that the person is not a regular resident (ashira) of that mosque.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
According to the text, he is not liable (la yadman). No diyah or compensation is required.
This is the preferred (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the mosque is built for prayer, and every Muslim has the right to pray alone or in congregation. Entrusting the organization of congregation to locals does not strip others of this right.
The act is permissible (mubah) and not transgressive.
4
Understand the Principle of Ta'addi
Liability requires transgression (ta'addi)—exceeding what is allowed. Since sitting in prayer is not transgressive, there is no liability.
Ta'addi is a key element in Hanafi tort law (diyat).
5
Consider Potential Contrasts
If the person had been sleeping or obstructing intentionally, the ruling may differ. This helps clarify the boundary of the rule.
The text implies that the sole focus on prayer keeps the act within permissible bounds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن جلس رجل من غير العشيرة فيه فى الصلاة فتعقل به إنسان ينبغى أن لا يضمن لأن المسجد بني للصلاة وأمر الصلاة بالجماعة إن كان مفوضا إلى أهل المسجد فلكل واحد من المسلمين أن يصلى فيه وحده
ترجمہ۔ اور اگر اہل مسجد کے غیر میں سے کوئی شخص مسجد میں بیٹھا ہو نماز میں پس اس سے کوئی انسان پھسل گیا تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ وہ ضامن نہ ہو اس لئے کہ مسجد نماز کے لئے بنائی گئی ہے اور نماز با جماعت کا کام ( نظم ) اگر چہ اہل مسجد کے سپرد ہے پس ہر مسلمان کے لئے یہ تو حق ہے کہ اس میں تنہا نماز پڑھے۔ تشریح کوئی دوسرا شخص جو اہل محلہ میں سے نہیں ہے مسجد میں نماز میں بیٹھا ہوا ہے جس کی وجہ سے کوئی پھسل کر مر گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہ ہو گا کیونکہ وہ نماز میں ہے اور مساجد نمازی کے لئے بنی ہیں۔ اور جماعت کا نظم تو اہل مسجد کے سپرد ہے لیکن اس میں نماز پڑھنا تو تمام مسلمانوں کے لئے درست ہے اور ہر ایک مسلمان کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ اس میں نماز پڑھ سکے تو وہ متعدی نہ ہوگا اور جب تعدی نہ ہوئی تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And if a man from other than the residents sits in it (the mosque) in prayer, and a person is tripped by him, it is appropriate that he is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer, and the matter of congregational prayer, even if entrusted to the residents of the mosque, every Muslim has the right to pray in it alone. Translation: And if a person other than the residents of the mosque sits in the mosque in prayer, and then a person slips due to him, it is appropriate that he is not liable because the mosque is built for prayer, and the organization of congregational prayer, even if entrusted to the residents, so every Muslim has the right to pray alone in it. Explanation: Another person who is not from the neighborhood is sitting in the mosque in prayer, and because of him someone slips and dies, then there is no liability on him because he is in prayer, and mosques are built for worshippers. And the organization of the congregation is entrusted to the residents, but praying in it is permissible for all Muslims, and every Muslim has the right to pray in it, so he is not a transgressor, and when there is no transgression, liability is not obligatory on him.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding liability for harm caused by a person sitting in the mosque in prayer. The issue is that a man who is not a regular resident of the mosque (i.e., not from the local congregation) sits in the mosque to pray, and someone trips over him or is otherwise harmed, and dies. According to the Hanafi school, this person is not liable for the damage because he was engaged in prayer, and the mosque is built for that purpose. The proof is that every Muslim has the right to pray in any mosque, even if the organization of the congregation is the responsibility of the local residents. Since he is not a trespasser or a transgressor (mut'addi), there is no liability. This ruling is based on the principle that an act that is inherently permissible (mubah) does not create liability unless done with transgression. The commentary explains that the lack of transgression (ta'addi) is key; thus, no diyah (blood money) is due.

Key Terms
متعدي (mut'addi): One who exceeds the bounds of what is permitted, causing liability.
ضمان (daman): Obligation to compensate for loss of life or property.
عشيرة (ashira): Residents, local community of the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person who is not a local resident sits in a mosque to pray and someone accidentally trips over him and dies, what is the ruling?
A) The person is liable because he caused harm.
B) The person is not liable because he was engaged in a permissible act (prayer) without transgression.
C) The person is liable only if he was sitting outside of prayer.
D) The person is liable because he should have been more careful.

Key Takeaway
No liability arises from a permissible act without transgression, even if harm occurs incidentally.

Liability for a Leaning Wall on a Public Pathway
Ruling on demolition and liability for a leaning wall causing harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for a leaning wall on a public path and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Negligence after warning transforms causation into transgression, imposing liability even without direct action.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on tort liability for a leaning wall that falls onto a public path. The text from al-Quduri presents a conflict between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) and shows how the Hanafi school prioritizes istihsan to impose liability on a negligent owner. Understanding this case illuminates how causation (tasbib) combined with transgression (ta'addi) can create liability even without a direct act.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify the baseline case (no warning) and the case with formal warning. In the baseline, the wall falls without any prior demand; in the second, the owner is formally warned to demolish and fails.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each
In the baseline, no liability. After warning and failure to demolish within a reasonable time, liability (daman) is wajib.
3
Examine the qiyas argument
Qiyas would say no liability because there is no direct action (mubasharat) by the owner; the leaning and falling are not his voluntary acts. The owner is like someone whose property causes harm without his involvement.
4
Apply istihsan
Istihsan overrides qiyas: the warning creates a duty to act. The owner's failure to demolish despite ability constitutes transgression (ta'addi) in causation (tasbib). Thus, he becomes liable.
5
Identify the legal principle
The principle is that liability can arise from causation (tasbib) when combined with negligence after notice. Direct action is not always required.

Section on the leaning wall. He (al-Quduri) said: And when a wall leans toward the road of the Muslims, and its owner is demanded to demolish it and witnesses are brought against him, and he does not demolish it within a time that he is able to, until it falls, he is liable for whatever is destroyed of life or property. The qiyas is that he is not liable because there is no direct act from him, nor is there a direct act of a condition in which he is transgressing, because the original building was in his property, and the leaning and occupying of airspace is not his act. So it is as before the attestation. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when a wall leans toward the road of the Muslims, then its owner is demanded to demolish it and witnesses are made against him, then he does not demolish it within the time he is able to, until it falls, then he is liable for what is lost of life or property. The qiyas is that he is not liable, because there is no direct act from him, nor is there a direct act of a condition in which he is transgressing, because the original building was in his property, and the leaning and occupying of airspace is not his act, so it becomes like before the attestation. Explanation: Someone's wall leaned, causing danger of falling. If no one said anything and the wall fell and someone died, he is not liable. But if someone who has a right of passage on that road tells him (in a commanding manner) and he still does not demolish it despite having sufficient time, and it falls and kills someone, then liability is obligatory upon him. This is the ruling of istihsan. Otherwise, the qiyas would require that no liability is obligatory, because there are two causes for liability: direct action (mubasharat) and causation (tasbib). Direct action is not present here, and causation is present to some degree but without transgression, and liability for causation is only...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof about a leaning wall on a public pathway. The matn from al-Quduri states that if a wall leans towards the path, the owner is asked to demolish it and witnesses are called. If he fails to demolish within a reasonable time and it falls causing harm, he is liable. The qiyas (analogical reasoning) would say no liability because there is no direct act (mubasharat) by the owner; the leaning is not his action. But the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to make him liable because he was negligent after being warned. The commentary explains the two bases of liability: direct action (mubasharat) and causation (tasbib). Here, there is causation but no transgression before the warning; after the warning, his failure to act becomes transgression (ta'addi) because he had the ability to prevent the harm. Therefore, he is liable. This ruling is based on istihsan overriding qiyas.

Key Terms
حائط مائل (ha'it ma'il): A wall that leans from its vertical position, posing a risk of collapse.
مباشرت (mubasharat): Direct physical action causing harm; one of the two bases for liability.
تسبیب (tasbib): Causation; indirect action that sets a chain of events leading to harm.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for reasons of equity or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a wall leans towards a public road and its owner is formally warned to demolish it but fails to do so within a reasonable time, and the wall falls and kills someone, what is the ruling?
A) The owner is not liable because he did not directly cause the harm.
B) The owner is liable because his failure to act after warning constitutes transgression (ta'addi) in causation.
C) The owner is liable only if he built the wall originally to be leaning.
D) The owner is not liable because the wall was on his property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tort law, causation (tasbib) combined with negligence after warning creates liability even without direct action.

Liability for Harm from a Leaning Wall: Diyah on Aqila, Property on Owner
Ruling on diyah and property compensation for harm from a leaning wall

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between liability for human deaths and property damage caused by a leaning wall, and identify the role of the aqila in paying diyah.

Core Idea
Diyah for human deaths is on the aqila; property compensation is on the owner's own wealth.

When a person is ordered to demolish a dangerous wall but fails, and the wall collapses causing harm, Islamic law distinguishes between lives lost and property destroyed. In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the ruling establishes that the blood money (diyah) for any deaths is borne by the aqila (the male agnates), while compensation for property damage comes from the owner's personal wealth. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction and the conditions required for liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its liability
Determine what harm occurred: human death or property damage. Both arise from the same act (failure to demolish after order), but the liability differs.
The condition is that the owner was previously told and asked to demolish.
2
State the ruling for human deaths
For every human life lost, diyah is wajib (obligatory) and is borne by the aqila (the male agnate relatives of the owner).
The text says: 'Then for lives destroyed by it, diyah is obligatory and the aqila bear it.'
3
State the ruling for property damage
For any property destroyed (animals, goods, etc.), compensation is wajib from the owner's own wealth, not the aqila.
The aqila do not compensate property.
4
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The text gives the reason: this is a crime less severe than khata' (unintentional killing), so by priority method (first priority), it deserves leniency. Property is excluded because aqila do not cover property.
This reasoning supports the aqila's role as a form of social insurance for human life.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
Some schools may place full liability on the owner, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) based on the reasoning.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi tarjih is based on the principle of leniency.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability for harm caused by a leaning wall after the owner has been ordered to demolish it. It distinguishes between human deaths and property damage. For human deaths, the blood money (diyah) is obligatory and is borne by the aqila (the male agnate relatives of the liable person). The reasoning is that this type of homicide is considered a crime but less severe than accidental killing (khata'), so to avoid crushing the owner with full liability, the responsibility is spread among the aqila as a form of leniency. For property damage (e.g., livestock, goods), the compensation is taken from the owner's own wealth because the aqila do not cover property losses. The condition for liability in both cases remains that the owner had been previously ordered to demolish the wall; formal testimony (ishhad) is not required. The text then raises a question about why diyah is on the aqila, suggesting further elaboration, but the passage ends here.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money: financial compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.
عاقلہ (aqila): The male agnate relatives of the perpetrator who are liable to pay diyah in cases of unintentional homicide.
خطاء (khata'): Accidental or unintentional act causing harm, distinct from intentional (amd) or quasi-intentional (shibh amd).
ضمان (daman): Compensation or liability for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The state treasury (bayt al-mal)
D) The victim (no compensation)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, blood money (diyah) for unintentional homicide from a neglected building is borne by the aqila, while property damage is paid by the owner personally.

Liability from a Leaning Wall: Distinction Between Deaths and Property
Ruling on diyah and property compensation for harm from a leaning wall.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for diyah and property compensation from a leaning wall, identify the condition of prior notification, and explain the a fortiori rationale (qiyas awla) for placing diyah on the 'aqilah.

Core Idea
Deaths from a wall: diyah on 'aqilah; property damage: owner pays. Condition: prior notification.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a leaning wall that causes harm. The ruling distinguishes between loss of life and loss of property, assigning liability to different parties. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) uses a fortiori analogy to justify leniency for the wall owner in death cases, while property damages remain his responsibility. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying diyat rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of harm
The passage covers two categories: deaths (al-nufus) and property (al-amwal, e.g., animals and goods). Note that the ruling differs for each.
2
State the liability for each
For deaths, diyah is wajib and borne by the 'aqilah. For property, compensation (daman) is wajib on the owner's personal wealth.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (ta'lil) for deaths
The author uses a qiyas awla (a fortiori) argument: this act is a crime (jinayah) even less than accidental killing (khata'). Since khata' already receives leniency (diyah on 'aqilah), this lesser crime deserves leniency even more, to avoid ruining the owner (istisal).
The phrase 'bi al-tariq al-awla' indicates primary inference.
4
Understand why property compensation remains on the owner
The 'aqilah does not bear property liabilities ('aqilah la ta'qil al-mal). Therefore, property damages must be paid by the owner from his own wealth.
5
Note the condition for liability
Liability requires that the owner was previously approached (al-taqaddum ilayhi) and requested to demolish the wall, without needing formal testimony (ishhad).
The condition 'al-shart al-taqaddum ilayhi wa talab al-naqd minhu duna al-ishhad'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم فيما تلف به من النفوس تجب الدية وتتحملها العاقلة لأنه فى كونه جناية دون الخطأ فيستحق فيه التخفيف بالطريق الأولى كيلا يؤدى إلى استيصاله ولإحجاف به وما تلف به من الأموال كالدواب والعروض يجب ضمانها فى ماله لأن العواقل لاتعقل المال والشرط التقدم إليه وطلب النقض منه دون الإشهاد
Then regarding lives lost by it, the blood-money is obligatory and the 'aqilah bears it because it, in being a crime less than khata' (unintentional), becomes deserving of leniency by primary inference, so that it does not lead to his eradication and harshness. And regarding property lost by it, such as animals and goods, their compensation is obligatory in his wealth because the 'aqilah do not bear property, and the condition is prior notification to him and demand of demolition from him without testimony.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of harm caused by the leaning wall. If a person dies, full diyah (blood-money) is obligatory, but it is borne by the 'aqilah (the paternal male relatives of the wall owner), not the owner himself. The reason is that this act (failure to demolish leading to death) is a type of crime (jinayah) that is even less than accidental killing (khata') in criminality. Since khata' already receives leniency (diyah on 'aqilah), this lesser crime deserves leniency a fortiori (bi al-tariq al-awla). If the diyah were on the owner's personal wealth, it would destroy him (istisal). Therefore, the 'aqilah pays. However, for property damage (animals, goods), the compensation is on the owner's own wealth because the 'aqilah do not bear property damages. The condition for liability is that the owner was previously approached and asked to demolish the wall, without requiring testimony (ishhad).

Key Terms
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The group of paternal male relatives (clan or tribe) who collectively pay diyah for unintentional killings or comparable crimes.
الدية (al-diyah): The blood-money or compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.

Key Takeaway

Liability for a Wall Built Leaning from the Start
Ruling that initial leaning wall creates automatic liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a wall built leaning initially and apply the qiyas jaliy to similar cases of initial transgression.

Core Idea
Initial transgression creates strict liability without prior notice.

This lesson addresses a specific case: a wall that is built leaning from the very beginning. Unlike a wall that later becomes dangerous, the builder here is immediately liable for any damage it causes, even without prior testimony or warning. The reasoning rests on the concept of initial transgression (ta'addi), analogized to the well-known case of extending a window or balcony into a public path. Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi school defines liability for dangerous constructions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage addresses a wall built leaning from the start. Determine the ruling: what is the builder's liability for damages?
2
Locate the legal cause
Identify the rationale: why is the builder liable without prior testimony? Look for the phrase 'because the construction is transgression from the start'.
3
Trace the qiyas
The ruling is analogized to ishra' al-janah. Identify the original case (asl), the new case (far'), and the shared cause (illa) – the act of construction itself being a transgression.
The illa here is jaliyyah (obvious), extracted through tanqih al-manat.
4
Contrast with a wall that later becomes leaning
Consider the opposite scenario: a wall built straight that later leans. How would the ruling differ? The passage implies that prior notification would be required in that case.
This contrast highlights the importance of the initial state.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Take a hypothetical: a contractor installs a heavy sign on a public road that is immediately unsafe. Does this ruling apply? Extend the qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو بنى الحائط مائلا في الابتداء قالوا يضمن ما تلف بسقوطه من غير إشهاد لأن البناء تعد ابتداء كما في إشراع الجناح
He said: If one built a wall leaning from the beginning, they (the scholars) said: he guarantees what is destroyed by its fall without testimony, because the construction is transgression from the start, just as in the case of extending a window (into a public path).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage covers an exceptional scenario. If a person builds a wall that is already leaning from the very beginning (as opposed to a wall that later leans due to age or weather), the builder is immediately liable for any damage caused by its collapse, even without prior testimony or demand for demolition. The reason is that the very act of building such a wall is a transgression (ta'addi) from the outset, because it encroaches on the public path or creates a danger. This is analogized (qiyas) to the case of 'ishra' al-janah' (extending a protruding window or balcony into a public thoroughfare), where mere construction is an encroachment. Therefore, liability does not require a prior notification or testimony; the builder is automatically a guarantor (damin).

Key Terms
إشراع الجناح (ishra' al-janah): Extending a window, balcony, or other structure into a public thoroughfare, which is considered a trespass.
تعد (ta'addi): Transgression or encroachment; a wrongful act that violates another's right or public property.
ضمان (damān): Liability to compensate for damage or loss; guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the wall leans after many years
B) If the wall was built leaning from the start
C) If the wall was built on his own property
D) If the wall is less than ten cubits high

Key Takeaway
The builder of a wall that is leaning from initial construction is automatically liable for damages without prior testimony, because the act of building itself is a transgression.

The Purpose and Valid Timing of Witnessing a Pre-Warning
Explains why witnessing is prescribed and when it is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of witnessing (ishhad) for a pre-warning and identify the condition for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Witnessing is a precaution, not a condition—it secures proof when the wall owner denies the warning.

In cases of dangerous leaning walls, the owner must be warned before liability attaches. But what if he later denies the warning? The Hanafi jurists prescribe a formal witnessing (ishhad) as a precautionary measure. This lesson unpacks the rationale and the precise timing: the wall must already be inclined for the witnessing to be legally meaningful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'ishhad'—formal witnessing of the pre-warning to demolish a dangerous wall. The ruling is not obligatory but recommended (mustahabb) as a precaution.
Liabilities in Hanafi law are not dependent on witnessing, but it is strongly encouraged.
2
Understand the purpose (talil)
The purpose is purely evidential: to enable the warning-giver to prove the warning in court if the owner denies it. Thus it falls under the principle of ihtiyat (precaution).
This is a practical reasoning (talil) from the text.
3
Learn the form (sighah) of witnessing
The witness must explicitly say: 'Bear witness that I have previously warned this man to demolish this wall of his.' The testimony must clearly state the prior warning.
The exact wording matters for legal proof.
4
Identify the condition for validity
Witnessing is not valid before the wall actually inclines. Before inclination, there is no transgression (ta'addi) to be prevented, so the warning is premature.
The wall must be in a dangerous state for the warning to be actionable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و إنما ذكر الإشهاد ليتمكن من إثباته عند أنكاره فكان من باب الاحتياط وصورة الإشهاد أن يقول الرجل اشهدوا أني قد تقدمت إلى هذا الرجل فى هدم حائطه هذا ولا يصح الإشهاد قبل أن يهى الحائط لانعدام التعدى
And he mentioned witnessing only so that he may be able to prove it when he denies it, so it is a precautionary measure. The form of witnessing is that the man says: 'Bear witness that I have previously warned this man to demolish this wall of his.' And witnessing is not valid before the wall inclines, due to the absence of transgression.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explaining the rationale behind the requirement of witnessing (ishhad) for the pre-warning (tawqif) to demolish a dangerous wall. The author clarifies that the purpose is not a legal condition but a precaution: it enables the warning-giver to prove the warning in court if the wall owner denies it. The valid moment for witnessing is after the wall has actually inclined, because before that there is no transgression (ta'addi) to be prevented. The witnessing phrase must explicitly state the prior warning. This follows the Hanafi principle of precaution in matters of liability.

Key Terms
إشهاد (ishhad): Formal witnessing of a pre-warning to a wall owner to demolish his leaning wall.
تقدم (taqaddum (here: tawqif)): The pre-warning given to the wall owner to demolish the dangerous wall.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is witnessing (ishhad) for a pre-warning to demolish a wall valid?
A) Before the wall inclines, so that the warning is on record.
B) After the wall inclines, because only then is there transgression.
C) At any time, as long as the witness remembers the warning.
D) Only if the wall has already collapsed.

Key Takeaway
Witnessing the pre-warning is a recommended precaution for proof, valid only after the wall has actually inclined and using the prescribed wording.

Liability for a Wall Built Leaning from the Start
States the ruling for a wall built leaning originally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish cases where liability arises immediately (without warning) from those requiring a warning, using the Hanafi concept of initial transgression (ta'addi ibtida').

Core Idea
A wall built leaning from the start is an initial transgression; liability for its fall is immediate without warning.

What happens when a person builds a wall that is visibly leaning from the moment it is erected? Does he get a chance to fix it before being held liable for any damage? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses exactly that scenario, drawing a clear analogy to a protruding balcony. The ruling rests on the nature of the act: if the construction itself is a transgression, the usual requirement of a warning is dropped.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
State the specific case: a wall built leaning from the start. The ruling is that the builder is liable for damages caused by its fall without any prior warning.
2
Identify the principle: initial transgression
Recognize that the Hanafi scholars considered the act of building a leaning wall as ta'addi (transgression) from the very beginning. This is key because transgression triggers liability even without warning.
Contrast with a wall that was originally straight but later became leaning — there, warning is required.
3
Compare with the analogous case
The text explicitly compares this to ishra' al-janah (protruding a balcony into public space without permission). Both are inherently transgressive acts that cause undue risk to others.
The analogy (qiyas) is made explicit in the source.
4
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The illa is 'initial transgression' (ta'addi ibtida'). In both cases, the act itself is unlawful from the outset, so liability is immediate.
This illa is jaliyyah (clear) and extracted via tanqih al-manat.
5
Apply the ruling and note the practical difference
The ruling is liability without warning. The practical difference (thamarah) from a non-transgressive wall is that in the latter, the builder must be warned and given a chance to demolish before being liable.
This lesson reinforces the Hanafi maxim: 'Al-ta'addi yujibu al-daman' (transgression necessitates liability).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو بنى الحائط مائلا في الابتداء قالوا يضمن ما تلف بسقوطه من غير إشهاد لأن البناء تعد ابتداء كما في إشراع الجناح
He said: If he built the wall leaning from the beginning, they (the scholars) said: He is liable for what is destroyed by its fall without warning, because the construction is transgression from the start, like in the case of protruding a balcony.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on liability for damage caused by a wall that was built leaning from the start. The author cites the consensus of the mashayikh (senior scholars) that the builder is liable for all damage caused by the fall, even if no warning was given. The reason is that building a wall in a leaning state is itself an act of transgression (ta'addi) from the outset, similar to projecting a balcony (ishra' al-janah) into public space without permission. Therefore, the usual requirement of a warning is waived. This follows the Hanafi principle that initial transgression establishes liability immediately.

Key Terms
إشراع الجناح (ishra' al-janah): Protruding a balcony or similar structure into a public pathway without authorization.
تعدى (ta'addi): Transgression; unlawful act that causes harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person builds a wall that is leaning from the start, and it falls causing damage, what is the ruling?
A) He is not liable because no warning was given.
B) He is liable without warning because the construction itself is transgression.
C) He is liable only if he refuses to demolish after warning.
D) He is liable only if the wall was originally straight and then leaned.

Key Takeaway
A wall built leaning from the start is an initial transgression; liability for its collapse is immediate without any requirement of warning.

Condition of Sufficient Time and Right to Demand Demolition
Sets conditions for liability and standing to demand removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of sufficient time before liability for a dangerous wall and identify who may demand its demolition.

Core Idea
A wall owner must be given time to demolish; every user of the path can demand its removal.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario where a person erects a wall that leans dangerously into a public pathway. The Hanafi school sets two key rules: first, the owner cannot be held liable unless given adequate time to demolish it; second, the right to demand demolition belongs to every individual who uses the path. Understanding these rules ensures fairness for the owner and protection for the public.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
Find the statement that a period (mudda) sufficient for demolition must be given. This is a condition (shart) for the owner to become a transgressor (jani).
The phrase 'wa sharta al-tark fi mudda yaqdiru 'ala naqdihi fiha' is the key.
2
Identify the second ruling
Find the statement that any Muslim or dhimmi, man or woman, free or mukatib can demand demolition. The reason given is that all people are partners (shuraka') in the right of passage.
The phrase 'yastawi an yutalibahu bi-naqdihi muslimun wa dhimmi' shows inclusivity.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Examine the two ta'lil phrases: (a) 'because possibility of demolition is necessary' – without sufficient time, the owner cannot comply, so liability is unfair; (b) 'because all people are partners in passing' – each individual has a personal right to the path, so each can enforce its clearance.
This ta'lil connects the ruling to its underlying rationale, essential for applying it analogously.
4
Apply the rulings to a concrete scenario
Take a case: a wall leans into a market. The owner is given 7 days (reasonable) but fails. A passing woman complains to the local mayor. Determine: Is the owner liable? Is the woman's demand valid?
The answer: owner becomes a transgressor after the period; the woman's demand is valid regardless of gender or authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط الترك في مدة يقدر على نقضه فيها لأنه لابد من إمكان النقض ليصير بتركه جانيا ويستوى أن يطالبه بنقضه مسلم و ذمى لأن الناس كلهم شركاء فى المرور فيصح التقدم إليه من كل واحد منهم رجلا كان أو امرأة حرا كان أو مكاتبا ويصح التقدم إليه عند السلطان وغيره لأنه مطالبة بالتفريغ فيتفرد كل صاحب حق به
And he stipulated delaying (the demolition) for a period in which he is able to demolish it, because the possibility of demolition is necessary so that by his leaving it he becomes a transgressor. And it is equal whether a Muslim or a dhimmi demands its demolition, because all people are partners in passing. So the pre-warning is valid from every one of them, whether man or woman, free or mukatib. And the pre-warning is valid before the sultan or other than him, because it is a demand to remove the obstruction, so every right-holder has exclusive standing.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, the wall owner must be given a period of time sufficient to actually demolish the wall. This is a necessary condition for liability: the owner becomes a transgressor only if he fails to demolish within a reasonable time after warning. Second, the right to demand demolition belongs to every person who uses the public pathway, regardless of religion (Muslim or dhimmi), gender, or status (free or mukatab). Even a slave in the process of manumission (mukatab) can make the demand. The demand can be made before any authority, not just a judge, because it is a right of every individual. The reasoning is that the pathway is common to all, so each has the right to demand its clearance.

Key Terms
مدة (mudda): A period of time sufficient for the owner to physically demolish the wall.
تفريغ (tafriqh): Removal of an obstruction from public space.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who can demand the demolition of a dangerous leaning wall in a public pathway?
A) Only the sultan or judge.
B) Only Muslim men.
C) Any person (Muslim or dhimmi, man or woman, free or mukatib) who uses the pathway.
D) Only the owner of adjacent property.

Key Takeaway
A leaning wall owner must be given sufficient time to demolish; any user of the public path can demand its removal before any authority.

Right to Demand Demolition When Wall Leans Toward Private House
Specifies that only the house owner may demand demolition when wall leans toward a private residence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the persons who have the right to demand demolition of a leaning wall and explain the basis for their right.

Core Idea
The right to demand demolition belongs to the owner exclusively, but residents also share it because they occupy the house and its airspace.

This passage addresses a specific property dispute: when a wall leans toward a private house, who can demand its removal? The ruling distinguishes between the owner and residents, each having a different basis. Understanding this distinction clarifies the Hanafi approach to harm-based rights (haqq al-darar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Note the two categories mentioned: the owner (مالك الدار) and residents (سكان) of the house.
2
Owner's exclusivity
The text states the right is exclusively (خا صة) for the owner because the harm is specific to him.
This is the primary right.
3
Residents' secondary right
Residents also may demand demolition because they have an interest in removing anything that occupies the house or its airspace.
This is derived from the principle of removing encroachment.
4
Rationale linkage
Understand the basis: the right stems from specific harm (darar) to the property, and residents share in that harm.
This is a talil (legal reasoning) based on harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مال إلى دار رجل فالمطالبة إلى مالك الدار خاصة لان الحق له على الخصوص وإن كان فيها سكان لهم أن يطالبوه لأن لهم المطالبة بإزالة ما شغل الدار فكذا بإزالة ما شغل هواء ها
And if it (the wall) leans toward a man's house, then the right to demand belongs exclusively to the owner of the house, because the right is specifically his. And if there are residents in it, they also may demand him, because they have the right to demand removal of what occupies the house, similarly removal of what occupies its airspace.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on who can demand the demolition of a wall that leans toward a private house rather than a public pathway. In this case, the right to demand is exclusive to the owner of that house, because only he suffers harm. However, if there are tenants or residents living in the house, they also have the right to demand, because they have an interest in removing anything that encroaches upon the house or its airspace. This is a specific application of the principle that a right-holder for a particular harm has exclusive standing, while others who are affected also share it.

Key Terms
مالك الدار (malik al-dar): The owner of the house toward which the wall leans.
سكان (sukkan): Residents or tenants of the house, who also have a right to demand removal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wall leans toward a private house, who has the right to demand its demolition?
A) Only the house owner.
B) Any passerby.
C) The house owner and any residents living there.
D) Only the sultan.

Key Takeaway
The right to demand removal of a leaning wall belongs to the house owner and residents, based on the specific harm to the property and its airspace.

Right to Demand Removal of Leaning Wall and Effect of Delay by Private Owner
Ruling on demand for removal of leaning wall and validity of delay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who has the right to demand removal of a leaning wall in Hanafi law and explain the effect of a private owner's delay or release on the wall owner's liability.

Core Idea
The right to demand removal is private; only the affected owner can waive it.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a common property dispute: a wall that leans onto a neighbour's land. It distinguishes between private and public rights, clarifying who can demand demolition and whether granting a delay removes liability. Understanding this ruling helps prevent confusion between personal and communal claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the right-holder
Determine whether the wall leans toward a private property or a public road. For private property, the right belongs to the owner (or residents). For a public road, the right belongs to the Muslim community.
The affected party's right is specific and exclusive.
2
Recognize the effect of delay or release
If the right-holder (private owner or resident) grants the wall owner a delay or releases him from liability, that act is valid and removes the wall owner's liability for future damage.
The right-holder chooses to waive his personal claim.
3
Distinguish the public road scenario
When the wall leans toward a public road, no individual (including a judge) can validly grant a delay because the right belongs to all Muslims and cannot be waived by a single person.
The community's right is inalienable by individuals.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete example
Consider Zaid's wall leaning onto Khalid's house. Khalid delays demolition. Later the wall falls and damages Khalid's car. Since Khalid was the sole right-holder, his waiver is valid, so Zaid is not liable.
Contrast with the public road case where such waiver would be invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر دیوار جھک گئی کسی شخص کے گھر کی جانب تو مطالبہ خاص طور پر مالک دار کی طرف ہو گا اس لئے کہ حق خاص طور پر اسی کے لئے ہے اور اگر اس گھر میں بہت سے رہنے والے ہوں تو ان سب کو یہ حق ہے کہ وہ مطالبہ کریں اس لئے کہ ان کو چیز کے مطالبہ کا حق ہے جو گھر کو مشغول کر دے پس ایسے ہی اس چیز کے ازالہ کا جو گھر کی فضا کو مشغول کردے۔ تشریح زید کے مکان کی دیوار اگر بجائے راستہ کے خالد کے گھر کی طرف جھک گئی ہو تو یہاں تو ڑوانے کا اختیار فقط خالد کو ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حق فقط اسی کا ہے۔ لیکن اگر وہ ایسی حویلی ہو جس میں بہت سے گھر ہوں تو ان میں سے ہر ایک کو یہ حق ہوگا کہ زید سے دیوار توڑنے کا مطالبہ کریں۔ کیونکہ ان لوگوں کو یہ حق ہے کہ اگر کسی کی کوئی چیز ان کے دار کو مشغول کرنے تو اس کے دور کرنے کا مطالبہ کریں۔ اسی طرح ان لوگوں کو یہ حق ہوگا کہ اس چیز کے دور کرنے کا مطالبہ کریں جو دار کی فضاء کو مشغول کر رہی ہے اور وہ یہاں زید کی دیوار ہے۔
مالک دیوار کو صاحب دار نے مہلت دی ، یا اسے بری کر دیا، یا اس کام کو دار کے رہنے والوں نے کیا ، صاحب دیوار پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا اگر کوئی چیز ہلاک ہوگئی
ولو أجله صاحب الدار أو أبرأه منها أو فعل ذالك ساكنوها فذالك جائز ولاضمان علیه فیما تلف بالحائط لأن الحق لهم بخلاف ما إذا مال إلى الطريق فأجله القاضى أو من أشهد عليه حيث لا يصح لأن الحق لجماعة المسلمين وليس إليهما إبطال حقهم.
ترجمہ اور اگر اس کو ( مالک دیوار کو) صاحب دار نے مہلت دے دی ہو یا اس کو اس سے بری کر دیا ہو یا اس کام کو دار کے رہنے والوں نے کیا ہو تو یہ جائز ہے اور صاحب دیوار پر ضمان نہ ہو گا اس چیز کے سلسلے میں جو دیوار سے تلف ہوئی ہے اس لئے کہ حق انہیں کا ہے، بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ دیوار راستہ کی طرف جھکی ہو پس قاضی نے اس کو مہلت دیدی ہو یا اس شخص نے جس نے اس پر ( صاحب مسلمین کا ہے، اور ان دونوں کی طرف ( قاضی اور اشہاد کرنے والا )
پر
دیوار پر اشہاد کیا ہے تو یہ مہلت دینا صحیح نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ حق تو ہوگا ان کے حق کو باطل کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ تشریح خالد کے گھر کی طرف زید کی دیوار بھی تھی اور خالد نے زید کو مہلت دیدی تو صحیح ہے یا حویلی والوں نے مہلت دے دی تو صحیح ہے اور اگر دیوار گرنے سے کچھ ہلاک ہو جائے تو دونوں صورتوں میں خالد پر ضمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جن لوگوں کا حق تھا انہوں نے مہلت دی تھی اور ان کو مہلت دینے کا حق تھا۔ اور اگر زید کی دیوار راستہ پر جھکی ہو اور مہلت دینے والا قاضی ہو یاوہ شخص جو اس سے اس کے توڑنے کا مطالبہ کر رہا ہے اور مطالبہ کرنے پر گواہ بنا رہا ہے تو ان کا مہلت دینا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہاں یہ ان کا حق نہیں ہے بلکہ مسلمین کا حق ہے اور ان کو جماعت مسلم کے حق کو باطل کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔
And if a wall leans toward a specific person's house, then the demand is specifically directed at the owner of the house, because the right belongs specifically to him. And if there are many residents in that house, they all have the right to demand, because they have the right to demand removal of something that occupies their house, just as they have the right to demand removal of something that occupies its airspace. Explanation: If Zaid's wall leans toward Khalid's house instead of the road, then only Khalid has the authority to have it demolished, because the right is only his. But if it is a large compound with many houses, each resident has the right to demand that Zaid demolish the wall, because they have the right to demand removal of anything that occupies their abode. Similarly, they have the right to demand removal of anything occupying the airspace of the abode, and here it is Zaid's wall. When the owner of the house gives the wall owner a delay, or releases him from liability, or the residents do this, then there is no liability on the wall owner if anything is destroyed. (Arabic text:) And if the owner of the house gives him a delay, or releases him from it, or the residents do that, then that is permissible, and there is no liability on him for what is destroyed by the wall, because the right is theirs. Contrary to the case where it leans toward the road, and the judge gives him a delay, or the person who witnesses against him, it is not valid, because the right belongs to the entire Muslim community, and they do not have the authority to nullify their right. Translation: And if the owner of the house gives him (the wall owner) a delay, or releases him from it, or the residents do that, then it is permissible, and the wall owner has no liability for what is destroyed by the wall, because the right is theirs. Contrary to the case where the wall leans toward the road, and the judge gives him a delay, or the person who witnesses against him, then this giving of delay is not valid, because the right belongs to the Muslim community, and they do not have the authority to nullify their right. Explanation: Khalid's house had Zaid's wall leaning toward it, and Khalid gave Zaid a delay — that is valid; or the residents of the compound gave a delay — that is valid. And if something is destroyed by the wall falling, in both cases Khalid has no liability, because those who had the right gave the delay, and they had the right to give it. But if Zaid's wall leans toward the road, and the one giving the delay is the judge or the person who was demanding its demolition and had witnesses made, then their giving a delay is not valid, because here it is not their right; the right belongs to the Muslim community, and they do not have the authority to nullify their right.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage presents two connected rulings from the Hanafi school on the liability for a leaning wall. First, it establishes that the right to demand demolition of a wall that leans into private property belongs exclusively to the owner of that property (or all residents if it is a shared dwelling). The wall owner is obligated to respond to their demand. Second, if the affected party voluntarily grants the wall owner a delay or legally releases him from responsibility, this is valid and the wall owner incurs no liability for any subsequent damage. The reasoning is that the right to demand removal belongs to the affected party, and they may waive it. However, this principle does not apply when the wall leans toward a public road. In that case, the right belongs to the entire Muslim community, so neither the judge nor any individual has the authority to waive it. The commentary illustrates both scenarios with the example of Zaid and Khalid, and warns against the confusion of treating a public right as a private one.

Key Terms
مہلت (muhlat): A delay granted by the affected party to the wall owner, allowing him time before demolishing the leaning wall.
ابراء (ibra'): A legal release from liability; here, the affected party releases the wall owner from any responsibility for future damage from the wall.
ضمان (daman): Liability or responsibility for damage or loss; in this context, the financial liability for damage caused by the wall's collapse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if Zaid's wall leans toward Khalid's private house, and Khalid gives Zaid a delay to demolish it, what is the ruling on Zaid's liability if the wall later falls and damages property?
A) Zaid remains fully liable because the right belongs to the community.
B) Zaid is not liable because Khalid, the right-holder, waived his right by granting the delay.
C) Zaid is liable only if the damage occurs after a specific time period.
D) Zaid's liability is transferred to Khalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a private property owner can validly waive the right to demand removal of a leaning wall, removing the wall owner's liability; but no individual can waive the community's right when the wall endangers a public road.

Liability for Leaning Wall After Sale: Seller Discharged, Buyer Warned
Ruling on liability of seller and buyer after warning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the liability of a seller who sells a property after being warned about a dangerous wall, and distinguish when the buyer becomes liable based on warning and ability.

Core Idea
Liability for failing to demolish ends when the owner sells because ability (tamakkun) is lost.

When a wall is dangerously leaning and the owner has been warned with witnesses, his liability arises from his inaction while having the ability to act. But what if he sells the property before demolishing? Does the liability transfer to the buyer? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling grounded in the principle of tamakkun (ability), and contrasts it with a case of a permanent nuisance like a projecting balcony. This lesson unpacks the rule and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the warning
The wall owner has been formally warned (ishhad) about the leaning wall. The act in question is selling the property after this warning.
Ishhad is a legal notice that establishes knowledge and triggers liability for inaction.
2
Determine liability of the seller
The seller is discharged because his ability to demolish (tamakkun) ends with the sale. Liability for omission requires ability; selling removes control, hence no liability.
This is the core ruling: liability is based on the ability to act.
3
Determine liability of the buyer
The buyer is not liable unless a new warning is made after purchase. Without warning, he has no duty and no liability for the pre-existing hazard.
The buyer's liability begins only from the moment he is warned and has ability.
4
Contrast with a projecting balcony
If the owner had created a permanent nuisance by construction (e.g., a projecting balcony), selling does not erase his liability because the harm is in the very placement, which is not undone by sale.
This distinction shows the difference between omission (tark) and positive act (wad').
5
Apply to a concrete example
Khalid's wall leans, he is warned, then sells to Bakr. Khalid is free; Bakr is free unless warned after purchase. If warned post-purchase and Bakr fails to act, he becomes liable.
This solidifies the rule in a familiar scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توجہ دلانے اور مطالبہ کرنے کے بعد دیوار مالک نے بیچ دی تو اب دیوار کی خرابی کا ذمہ دار کون ہوگا ، کیا خریدار کے سامنے مطالبہ بھی ضروری ہوگا

After giving attention and demanding, the wall owner sold the property. Now who will be responsible for the wall's defect? Is demand also necessary before the buyer? (Arabic text:) And if he sells the house after having witnesses made against him, and the buyer takes possession, he (the seller) is discharged from his liability because the offense is abandoning demolition while having the ability, and his ability is removed by the sale, contrary to the case of projecting a balcony (إشراع الجناح) because he was an offender by the very placement, and the placement is not invalidated by sale, so he is not discharged, as we have mentioned. And there is no liability on the buyer because no witnesses were made against him. And if witnesses are made against him after his purchase, then he is liable for abandoning clearance while having the ability after being demanded. Translation: And if he sells the house after having witnesses made against him, and the buyer takes possession, he is discharged from his liability because the offense is abandoning demolition while having the ability, and his ability is removed by the sale, contrary to the case of projecting a balcony because he was an offender by the placement, and the placement is not invalidated by sale, so he is not discharged, according to the detail we have mentioned. And there is no liability on the buyer because no witnesses were made against him. And if witnesses are made against the buyer after his purchase, then he is liable for abandoning clearance while having the ability, after having been demanded. Explanation: Khalid's wall was leaning, and demand had been made for its demolition, but Khalid sold this house to Bakr. Now there is no liability on Khalid because he is no longer the owner and has no right to demolish. And there is also no liability on Bakr because no demand was made on him. Yes, if after purchase, demand is made on him and he does not demolish, then liability becomes incumbent on him, because he now has the ability to demolish and has been demanded. However, if someone had installed a balcony or projection, since he was an offender from the beginning, selling the house does not discharge him from liability; rather, liability remains on him.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical issue in tort liability: what happens when a wall owner, who has been warned about a leaning wall, sells the property before acting. The Hanafi ruling draws a distinction between an omission (tark) and a positive act (wad'). In the case of a leaning wall, the wall owner's liability arises from his failure to demolish it while he had the ability (tamakkun). When he sells the house, he loses that ability because he no longer controls the property. Hence, his liability is extinguished. The buyer, however, is not liable unless he is specifically warned after purchase, because the liability attaches only from the moment of warning and ability. This is contrasted with the case of a projecting balcony (إشراع الجناح): the owner created a permanent nuisance by construction (wad'), so selling does not erase his original liability — he remains responsible even after transfer. The commentary provides a clear example: Khalid sells to Bakr; Khalid is free, Bakr is free unless warned post-purchase. This ruling teaches that liability for failing to act is personal to the one who can act, while liability for a positive harmful installation attaches to the original wrongdoer.

Key Terms
تمکن (tamakkun): The ability or capacity to perform an action; here, the wall owner's ability to demolish the wall before sale.
اشہاد (ishhad): The act of making witnesses; legal warning given to the wall owner or buyer in the presence of witnesses.
تفریغ (tafriqh): Emptying or clearing; here, the act of demolishing the leaning wall to clear the danger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wall owner is formally warned about a leaning wall. He sells the house to a buyer. The buyer is not warned. The wall collapses. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, who is liable?
A) The seller is liable.
B) The buyer is liable.
C) Neither the seller nor the buyer is liable.
D) Both are jointly liable.

Key Takeaway
Liability for failing to act on a warning is personal and requires both ability (tamakkun) and warning at the time of inaction; sale extinguishes the seller's ability and does not automatically transfer liability.
